![](images/5200b2c569bd868cbb40a1d143d894588b7a3d81964ca9f325d9495b8322ab95.jpg)

![](images/94c21db3f1c0aeb055302f4e10c5fb79686a396c95ec898b5db1d5224f9abece.jpg)

# IDENTIFICATION SERIAL NUMBER

The outboard motor’s serial number is stamped on a label which is attached to the port side of the clamp bracket.

# NOTE:

If the serial number label is removed, “VOID” marks will be appear on the label.

$\textcircled{1}$ Model name $\textcircled{2}$ Approved model code $\textcircled{3}$ Transom height $\textcircled{4}$ Serial number

The starting serial number blocks are as follows:

# SAFETY WHILE WORKING

The procedures given in this manual are those recommended by Yamaha to be followed by Yamaha dealers and their mechanics.

![](images/8d3cfaaae89e65c26f369c4e1303016cbb0bb5e22b59f47b0157003b89134bee.jpg)

# FIRE PREVENTION

Gasoline (petrol) is highly flammable. Petroleum vapor is explosive if ignited. Do not smoke while handling gasoline and keep it away from heat, sparks and open flames.

![](images/819d2138a3511b4f9f624361105c28483b20e77768d208355021c3b36f713230.jpg)

# VENTILATION

Petroleum vapor is heavier than air and is deadly if inhaled in large quantities. Engine exhaust gases are harmful to breathe. When test-running an engine indoors, maintain good ventilation.

![](images/723f8f33a7a4a4498cedda57c98a7402bdec83cf55e7ec9724859f3de1420408.jpg)

# SELF-PROTECTION

Protect your eyes with suitable safety glasses or safety goggles, when grinding or when doing any operation which may cause particles to fly off. Protect hands and feet by wearing safety gloves or protective shoes if appropriate to the work you are doing.

![](images/2c04f0fd3fcae74d3ddaaed4b8d86d7eb33c6f5ccd516ff61d208f1826ff96e0.jpg)

# OILS, GREASES AND SEALING FLUIDS

Use only genuine Yamaha oils, greases and sealing fluids or those recommended by Yamaha.

Under normal conditions of use, there should be no hazards from the use of the lubricants mentioned in this manual, but safety is all-important, and by adopting good safety practices, any risk is minimized. A summary of the most important precautions is as follows:

1. While working, maintain good standards of personal and industrial hygiene.   
2. Clothing which has become contaminated with lubricants should be changed as soon as practicable, and laundered before further use.   
3. Avoid skin contact with lubricants; do not, for example, place a soiled wipingrag in your pocket.   
4. Hands and any other part of the body which have been in contact with lubricants or lubricant-contaminated clothing, should be thoroughly washed with hot water and soap as soon as practicable.   
5. To protect the skin, the application of a suitable barrier cream to the hands before working, is recommended.   
6. A supply of clean lint-free cloths should be available for wiping purposes.

![](images/a1216c6601fc84bebae27a7a905dbfb269ce1eb0c6deeae5a56a605e1cbd9f9b.jpg)

# GOOD WORKING PRACTICES

1. The right tools Use the recommended special tools to protect parts from damage. Use the right tool in the right manner – do not improvise.

2. Tightening torque

Follow the tightening torque instructions. When tightening bolts, nuts and screws, tighten the large sizes first, and tighten inner-positioned fixings before outer-positioned ones.

![](images/08ec1b8a07474ff46681c5b35f9c114def0cb6bb29c3230b2d1d85d332c0626b.jpg)

![](images/314e6bb544e9e3eaf7ea1f2ab10df0752cdea4ec72ce322f5326ca5e12ecb6c9.jpg)

![](images/40232448e4959582fedcb284cc872b6ceee09dcff76e9f8f20bc7cecb52e6e90.jpg)

3. Non-reusable items Always use new gaskets, packings, Orings, split-pins, circlips, etc., on reassembly.

# DISASSEMBLY AND ASSEMBLY

1. Clean parts with compressed air when disassembling.   
2. Oil the contact surfaces of moving parts before assembly.

3. After assembly, check that moving parts operate normally.

4. Install bearings with the manufacturer’s markings on the side exposed to view, and liberally oil the bearings. 5. When installing oil seals, apply a light coating of water-resistant grease to the outside diameter.

![](images/498bd140b89b599061bca534c339813a7f725aeb4ff70b83bbf6ddac36adee2a.jpg)

# SPECIAL TOOLS

Using the correct special tools recommended by Yamaha, will aid the work and enable accurate assembly and tune-up. Improvising and using improper tools can damage the equipment.

# NOTE:

• For U.S.A. and Canada, use part numbers that start with “J-”, “YB-”, “YM-”, “YU-” or “YW-”.   
• For others countries, use part numbers that start with $" 9 0 8 9 0 \cdot ^ { \prime \prime }$ .

# GENERAL TORQUES

This chart specifies tightening torques for standard fasteners with a standard ISO thread pitch. Tightening torque specifications for special components or assemblies are provided in applicable sections of this manual. To avoid warpage, tighten multifastener assemblies in a crisscross fashion and progressive stages until the specified tightening torque is reached. Unless otherwise specified, tightening torque specifications require clean, dry threads. Components should be at room temperature.

# TOP COWLING CHECKING THE TOP COWLING FIT

![](images/50f3c3769291361ca893beefc64445228af456ca4f73fc08a33e2655b6fd0a25.jpg)

1. Check:   
• Top cowling fitting Loose/unlatched Adjust the top cowling hook.

# 2. Adjust:

• Top cowling hook position

# Adjustment steps

(1) Loosen the bolts $\textcircled{1}$ .   
(2) Move the top cowling hook $\textcircled{2}$ either up or down slightly (only a few millimeters).   
(3) Secure the bolts.   
(4) Check the top cowling fitting and repeat the adjustment if necessary.

# NOTE:

• Moving the latch towards the seal will loosen the top cowling.   
• Moving the latch away from the seal will tighten the top cowling.

![](images/01f9adc95c40a6af7207d4c891afa490b314a0a1bd9bd151f481dbcf17c7bcd1.jpg)

# FUEL SYSTEM CHECKING THE FUEL LINE

1. Check: • High-pressure fuel line Cracks/damage/leaks Replace. Refer to “HIGH-PRESSURE FUEL LINE” on page 4-8.

![](images/b4fe02edcf24f86c50b17f86e426d756f8351b5d58ebca0156e44bb38a6e234c.jpg)

![](images/2193dfc430506d552fc85761111689c4f8d92edce98e35d8679c912b4f26dee7.jpg)

![](images/52ca1fdd3e08ce790f80c68e6e0164c467f9077ec861b2749b4662ef5d136b2e.jpg)

2. Check:

• Plastic locking tie Loosen Retighten or replace.

3. Check:

• Low-pressure fuel line   
Cracks/damage/leaks Replace.   
Refer to “LOW-PRESSURE FUEL LINE” on page 4-26.

# CHECKING THE FUEL FILTER

Check:

• Fuel filter element   
• Fuel filter cup Clogs/cracks/leaks Replace. Foreign matter Clean.   
Refer to “FUEL FILTER” on page 4-29.

# MEASURING THE FUEL PRESSURE(HIGH-PRESSURE FUEL LINE)

Measure:

• Fuel pressure (high-pressure fuel line) Out of specification Check the highpressure fuel line.

![](images/8f1eeec6291da81d70b87ff1250e3722a0ea934eec7cd194a1c157c273e9ee20.jpg)

Fuel pressure (high-pressure fuel line) 300 kPa (3.0 kg/cm2, 44.1 psi)

# Measuring steps

(1) Install the fuel pressure gauge onto the pressure check valve.

![](images/6413fbb773345c97d6e93778a1d627b3f04dd4dd4fafdc35a680e4b6b9fe6a93.jpg)

(2) Turn the main switch to on, and then measure the fuel pressure.

![](images/92d0a99e6e9b6aabb071533a8c7eed52169008e04a74053ca0d7fcd75ccfef96.jpg)

# CONTROL SYSTEM CHECKING AND ADJUSTING THE THROTTLE BODY PICKUP TIMING

1. Check: • Throttle body pickup timing Incorrect Adjust.

# Checking steps

(1) Turn the throttle control lever to the full retard position.   
(2) Check that the mark $\textcircled{2}$ on the throttle cam aligns with the center of the throttle roller $\textcircled{1}$ as shown.

![](images/fef46a1ab50ebe013238dbce0e95ae3968e60f970a850ab4e155fef5701ab9af.jpg)

# 2. Adjust:

• Throttle body pickup timing

# Adjustment steps

(1) Loosen the nut $\textcircled{1}$ . (2) Remove the throttle joint link rod $\textcircled{2}$ . (3) Move the throttle control lever $\textcircled{3}$ until it contacts the fully-closed stopper $\textcircled{4}$ .

# NOTE:

Make sure the throttle is fully-closed.

(4) Align the fully-closed mark $\textcircled{2}$ on the throttle control lever $\textcircled{3}$ with the center of the throttle roller $\textcircled{5}$ as shown.   
(5) Adjust the length of the throttle joint link rod until $\textcircled{6}$ is $0 . 5 ~ \mathsf { m m }$ .   
(6) Tighten the nut and install the throttle joint link rod onto the throttle control lever.   
(7) Move the throttle control lever to check that the throttle valve opens and closes smoothly. Also, make sure the throttle roller aligns with the fullyopen position $\circledcirc$ on the accelerator cam.   
(8) Set the throttle to the fully-closed position and check that the fully-closed mark $\textcircled{2}$ aligns with the center of the throttle roller.

![](images/efebe65e877763d6754512a0277b824c4d1d275f11b68880d835ff2f7c911f6f.jpg)

![](images/355bfcb7d09ca1046abfe8f2ce2a84c8979651993e01e00b82258d53a6983718.jpg)

![](images/fde571764553f30d3af9c61f0440cd6def3a3c3727515fd9d4d09a388e482ac2.jpg)

# ADJUSTING THE SHIFT CABLE

1. Check: • Shift operation Incorrect Adjust.

2. Adjust: • Shift cable joint position

# Adjustment steps

(1) Align the mark $\textcircled{2}$ on the bushing with the mark $\textcircled{6}$ on the bracket $\circledcirc$ .   
(2) Loosen the locknut $\textcircled{1}$ and remove the clip $\textcircled{2}$ .   
(3) Remove shift cable joint $\textcircled{3}$ from the set pin.   
(4) Position the remote control lever in the neutral position.   
(5) Adjust the position of the shift cable joint until it aligns with the set pin.

# WARNING

# The shift cable joint must be screwed in at least 8 mm (0.31 in).

(6) Install the shift cable joint onto the set pin.   
(7) Install the clip and tighten the locknut.   
(8) Move the remote control lever to the forward, neutral, and reverse positions and make sure it shifts smoothly and correctly. If the shifting operation is unsmooth or incorrect, repeat the above procedure.

# 3. Check:

• Shift operation Unsmooth operation Repair.

![](images/7e28b3956df6fbeec82370a2427f273e44997382cdecb8b63424156199f5559b.jpg)

![](images/3745dc37f8a67ab4d0c1ec4fd5e05c7b627e1375e24729943813d18331e6cb2d.jpg)

# ADJUSTING THE THROTTLE CABLE

1. Check: • Fully closed position Incorrect Adjust.

# Checking steps

(1) Fully close the throttle. (2) Check that the throttle control lever $\textcircled{1}$ touches the fully-closed stopper $\textcircled{2}$ .

# 2. Adjust:

• Throttle cable joint position

# Adjustment steps

(1) Contact the throttle control lever $\textcircled{1}$ with the fully-closed stopper $\textcircled{2}$ .   
(2) Loosen the locknut $\textcircled{3}$ and remove the clip $\textcircled{4}$ .   
(3) Remove throttle cable joint $\textcircled{5}$ from the set pin $\textcircled{2}$ .   
(4) Position the remote control lever in the neutral position.   
(5) Adjust the position of the throttle cable joint until it aligns with the set pin.

# WARNING

The throttle cable joint must be screwed in at least 8 mm (0.31 in).

(6) Install the throttle cable joint onto the set pin.   
(7) Install the clip and tighten the locknut.   
(8) Open and close the throttle (at the remote control) several times and make sure the throttle valves open and close smoothly and correctly. If the throttle operation is unsmooth or incorrect, repeat the above procedure.

# ADJUSTING THE THROTTLE POSITION SENSOR

. Measure:   
• Throttle position sensor output voltage Out of specification Adjust.

Throttle position sensor output voltage (pink (P) – black (B)) 0.732 ± 0.014 V

# NOTE:

• Be sure to adjust the throttle valve’s opening before measuring the throttle position sensor output voltage.   
• When measuring the throttle position sensor output voltage, set the digital tester to the manual range.

![](images/ed5b2aa054167f6b74a5c01d18bf6a81684e6cc1746a8a55d97e8d12a90a76e8.jpg)

![](images/6dbc05f0369aad34197231b8354bee94476d0529f8380507e2d776211b980035.jpg)

# Measuring steps

(1) Remove the intake silencer. Refer to “INTAKE ASSEMBLY” on page 4-3.   
(2) Disconnect the throttle joint link rod $\textcircled{1}$ at the throttle body.   
(3) Check the throttle valve.   
(4) Connect the test harness (3-pin) as shown.

![](images/6dbedf66e2d6dcd89c501c01c586f251ad3e37d16dc93e67c552694bf33628c5.jpg)

# Test harness (3-pin) 90890-06793

(5) Connect the digital tester probes to the test harness (3-pin) as shown.   
(6) Turn the engine start switch on.   
(7) Measure the output voltage.   
(8) Install the intake silencer.   
(9) Start the engine and measure the output voltage again.

![](images/5c27f56e2f9b404a0d87145a731640a9c403a8108e760a22ac7148782a8d6dbf.jpg)

![](images/3798f7be24cba6c1999dbb122cc0f989b4a1edfe3eecf26f076864cc93f3281f.jpg)

2. Adjust:

• Throttle position sensor

# Adjustment steps

(1) Loosen the screws $\textcircled{2}$ .   
(2) Adjust the position of the throttle position sensor until the specified output voltage is obtained. (3) Tighten the screws.   
(4) Connect the throttle joint link rod $\textcircled{1}$ .

![](images/048804e739c94379f9fa211b460b0f57ec769e25b7707416ae3223d8c94ada7e.jpg)

# SYNCHRONIZING THE THROTTLE VALVES

# CAUTION:

Do not adjust the throttle valve when it is operating properly. Excess adjustment may cause poor engine performance.

# Adjustment steps

(1) Remove all of the blind plugs $\textcircled{1}$ . (2) Connect the adaptors $\textcircled{2}$ and vacuum gauge $\textcircled{3}$ to the intake manifold assembly as shown.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Vacuum gauge set YU-08030 / 90890-03094</td></tr></table>

(3) Start the engine and allow it to warm up for several minutes.   
(4) Connect the tachometer to the spark plug lead of cylinder #1.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Tachometer YU-08036-A ／ 90890-06760</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>Engine idling speed 750 ± 50 r/min</td></tr></table>

(5) Check the vacuum pressure of all cylinders.

(6) Turn the synchronizing screw $\textcircled{4}$ so the vacuum pressure of cylinder #3 or #4 is within 30 mmHg (40 mbar, 1.18 inHg) based of the vacuum pressure of cylinder #1 or #2.

<table><tr><td>Tighten</td><td>Vacuum pressure increases.</td></tr><tr><td>Loosen</td><td>Vacuum pressure decreases.</td></tr></table>

<table><tr><td>General adjusting tool</td></tr><tr><td>Torx T-25 (with a concave in the center)</td></tr></table>

![](images/38ae97adadfe5c3c0782beb3e4e098646088cedbd2d9c64e4a66c8e0f279bc8f.jpg)

![](images/b3e5bd7bb49e5b33524b489d3eb2367dac91519ea92adaabdac325b72c243948.jpg)

# ADJUSTING THE THROTTLEPOSITION SENSOR(WHEN DISASSEMBLING ORREPLACING THE THROTTLE BODY)

# Adjusting steps

(1) Install the intake assembly with the intake silencer removed.   
(2) Disconnect the throttle position sensor coupler.   
(3) Install the test harness to the throttle position sensor coupler.

<table><tr><td>o0</td><td>Test harness 90890-06793</td></tr></table>

(4) Connect the digital circuit tester.

<table><tr><td>0</td><td>Digital tester J-39299 / 90890-06752</td></tr></table>

(5) Turn the main switch to on.

(6) Loosen the synchronizing screw and fully open the lower side throttle valve (#3, 4).

(7) Loosen the idling screw $\textcircled{1}$ and fully close the upper side throttle valve (#1, 2).

(8) Adjust the position of the throttle position sensor until the output voltage is $0 . 7 \pm 0 . 0 1 \mathrm { \Delta V }$ and operate the throttle valve several times.

(9) Record the value.

(10) Slowly tighten the synchronizing screw $\textcircled{2}$ until the recorded value is changed.

(11) Slowly tighten the idling screw until $0 . 0 3 2 ~ \pm ~ 0 . 0 0 4 ~ \mathrm { ~ V ~ }$ increase over the recorded value.

(12) Operate the throttle valve several times.

(13) Install the throttle roller $\textcircled{8}$ as the mark $\textcircled{6}$ aligns with center of the throttle roller and check that the output voltage is not change.

(14) Install the intake silencer.

(15) Start the engine.

(16) If the output voltage of the throttle position sensor is not within $0 . 7 3 2 \ \pm$ $0 . 0 1 4 \ \vee$ , adjust the throttle position sensor.

(17) Check that the throttle valve is synchronized.

![](images/928a1d581624f7c30d9578213816530bb1fddb1ae03054bebff6aa8abfa7d5b6.jpg)

# COOLING SYSTEM CHECKING THE COOLING WATER DISCHARGE

Check:

• Cooling water discharge No discharge Clean and check the cooling water passage.

# Checking steps

(1) Place the lower unit in water.   
(2) Start the engine.   
(3) Check that water flows from the cooling water outlet.

![](images/bdfa6824aa406fed58d5aab96af208ac39560f57ac1ae1ce76a2367e5e387af6.jpg)

engine oil. Below $\textcircled { 6 }  \mathsf { A d d }$ engine oil so that the level is between $\textcircled{2}$ and $\textcircled{6}$ .

# CHECKING THE TIMING BELT

Check:

• Timing belt Wear/damage Replace.

![](images/201c8487300081f5e1f700ae1dbb1d82b5b423daecee5adac490483879e72491.jpg)

# ADJUSTING THE VALVE CLEARANCE

# NOTE:

Valve clearance adjustment should be made on a cold engine, at room temperature.

1. Remove:

• Flywheel magnet cover • Spark plug cap cover $\textcircled{1}$

2. Disconnect: • Spark plug leads $\textcircled{2}$ • Fuel hoses $\textcircled{3}$ • Ventilation hose • Vacuum hose

3. Loosen: • Timing belt tensioner

4. Remove: • Timing belt • Driven sprockets • Cylinder head cover • Spark plugs

5. Install:

• Driven sprockets • Timing belt

6. Tighten: • Timing belt tensioner

![](images/c715b3fb48d91853d18cd3f4f9a12780a19c1d8c10ff19239e245100358b8ba3.jpg)

7. Measure:

• Intake valve clearance $\textcircled{2}$ • Exhaust valve clearance $\textcircled{6}$

<table><tr><td></td><td>Valve clearance Intake 0.20 ± 0.03 mm (0.008 ± 0.001 in)</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

If any valve clearance is out of specification, record its measurement.

![](images/4a3a3e543c8ca7a61913cc23fa4dd5db9af413801b6249e560132049c13bad9c.jpg)

# Measurement steps

(1) Turn the flywheel magneto clockwise until cylinder #1’s piston is at TDC.   
(2) Measure the intake valve clearance for cylinders #1 and #2.   
(3) Measure the exhaust valve clearance for cylinders #1 and #3.   
(4) Turn the flywheel magneto $3 6 0 ^ { \circ }$ clockwise.   
(5) Measure the intake valve clearance for cylinders #3 and #4.   
(6) Measure the exhaust valve clearance for cylinders #2 and #4.

8. Loosen:

• Timing belt tensioner

9. Remove: • Timing belt • Driven sprockets • Camshaft caps • Camshafts Refer to “POWER UNIT” on page 5-4.

10. Adjust:

• Valve clearance

# NOTE:

• Do not mix the valve train parts (i.e., valve pads, camshaft caps, camshafts). Keep them organized in their proper groups (e.g., cylinder #1 parts kept together). • Install the removed parts in their original positions. If valve train parts are installed in the wrong position, proper valve adjustments are impossible.

# Adjustment steps

(1) Insert a thin screwdriver into the notch in the valve lifter.   
(2) Carefully pry up the valve pad and remove it.   
(3) Measure the thickness removed valve pad with a micrometer.   
(4) Select a proper replacement valve pad by calculating its thickness with the following formula.

# Proper valve pad thickness = Removed valve pad thickness $^ { + }$ Measured valve clearance – Specified valve clearance

(5) Install the proper valve pad into the valve lifter.

# NOTE:

• Measure the thickness of the new valve pad with a micrometer because the thickness number is not indicated on the pad.   
• Lubricate the valve pad with molybdenum disulfide grease.   
• Perform the above procedure for all valves whose clearances are out of specification.

11. Install:

• Camshafts • Camshaft caps • Driven sprockets • Timing belt

12. Tighten: • Timing belt tensioner Refer to “POWER UNIT” on page 5-4.

13. Recheck: • Valve clearance

NOTE:

If any valve clearance is still out of specification, repeat all of the valve clearance adjustment steps until the specified clearance is obtained.

![](images/4830b1e0e885f2ddb7e5547c280c897a0e9366f796376dca1398ffc53eaf2294.jpg)

14. Loosen: • Timing belt tensioner

15. Remove: • Driven sprockets • Timing belt

16. Tighten: • Timing belt tensioner

17. Install: • Cylinder head cover • Driven sprockets • Timing belt • Spark plugs

18. Connect: • Vacuum hose • Ventilation hose • Fuel hoses • Spark plug leads

19. Install:

• Spark plug cap cover • Flywheel magneto cover

# POWER TRIM AND TILT SYSTEM CHECKING THE POWER TRIM AND TILT FLUID LEVEL

Check: • Power trim and tilt fluid level Level is $\mathsf { l o w } \to \mathsf { A d d }$ power trim and tilt fluid to the proper level.

![](images/f4178042ed329cea0cb12a9168a6744d9f7afee314eee9334017dbe5f4c313ea.jpg)

# WARNING

When removing the power trim and tilt reservoir cap, the power trim and tilt fluid may spurt out due to internal pressure. Therefore, fully tilt up the outboard (the tilt ram assembly fully extended) and then slowly remove the power trim and tilt reservoir cap.

![](images/4b027cdbda743f2c12576ee2107cc8d968bd7fb99355da1742e5babc825161f2.jpg)

![](images/a5ec14cad96f164517ede9e69d782f9f4e534ca436abcefce19d97ed466693a0.jpg)

![](images/e56c55b880d336c6c3168a7160ca49ac60f316e46530b21e341e1b073a1437f8.jpg)

# Checking steps

(1) Tilt the outboard all the way up and lock it with the tilt stop levers $\textcircled{1}$ .

# WARNING

After tilting up the outboard, be sure to support it with the tilt stop levers. Otherwise, the outboard could suddenly lower if the power trim and tilt unit should lose fluid pressure.

(2) Remove the reservoir cap $\textcircled{2}$ and check the fluid level.

NOTE:

The fluid level should be directly below the check hole as shown.

(3) Add power trim and tilt fluid if needed, and then install the reservoir cap.

Reservoir cap 8 Nm (0.8 m • kgf, 5.8 ft • lb)

# ADJUSTING THE TRIM SENSOR CAM

1. Measure: • Trim sensor setting resistance Out of specification Adjust.

Trim sensor setting resistance Pink (P) – Black (B) ${ \bf 8 0 } \pm { \bf 1 2 } \Omega$ at $\ 20 \%$ (68 ˚F)

# Measuring steps

(1) Fully tilt the outboard down.   
(2) Measure the trim sensor resistance.

![](images/451a3533c7502960db5fcfa8f2720a74d9627119245c8be590164d496626cd74.jpg)

2. Adjust: • Trim sensor cam position

# Adjusting steps

(1) Fully tilt the outboard to full trim-in position.   
(2) Loosen the screw $\textcircled{1}$ .   
(3) Adjust the position of the trim sensor cam $\textcircled{2}$ until the specified resistance is obtained.

![](images/cc27bad3705b401b2e71680fcf67150699a3df1c13b816c2782758535fdf9742.jpg)

Trim sensor resistance Pink (P) – Black (B) ${ \bf 8 0 } \pm { \bf 1 2 } \Omega$ at 20 ˚C (68 ˚F)

(4) Tighten the screw.

![](images/2f39bf8ee6d8fa8acdb94fa19f8db345e5fff9419a45fd69c132ab440a247a8d.jpg)

• Gear oil level   
Level is l $\mathsf { o w } \to \mathsf { A }$ dd gear oil to the proper level.

# CHANGING AND CHECKING THE GEAR OIL

1. Check: • Gear oil Milky oil Replace the oil seal. Slag oil Check the gears, bearings, and clutch dog.

# Checking steps

(1) Tilt up the outboard slightly. (2) Place a container under the gear oil drain screw $\textcircled{1}$ . (3) Remove the gear oil drain screw and gear oil level check screw $\textcircled{2}$ .

2. Fill: • Gear oil (with the specified amount of the recommend gear oil)

![](images/d0454c98d03b704debbaed1c92f435cd8c2d14645699152c360dbb7c15e87be6.jpg)

![](images/c1811baa03392555e6066aea484a4529dc9501a9c3bed75f630e7169f24d5016.jpg)

# Filling steps

(1) Place the outboard in an upright position.   
(2) Insert the gear oil tube into the drain hole and slowly fill the gear oil until oil flows out of the check hole and no air bubbles are visible.   
(3) Install the gear oil level check screw and then quickly install the gear oil drain screw.

![](images/e9a6963b8f74eaa3ecdfbb3ab0093004d9e5b61a9854b8092a3b82cb4f179c8d.jpg)

# CHECKING THE LOWER UNIT(FOR AIR LEAKS)

Check: • Lower unit holding pressure Pressure drops Check the seals and components.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Lower unit holding pressure 100 kPa (1.0 kg/cm², 14.2 psi)</td></tr></table>

![](images/374ff3c568a6cab8fb4b9d6635469ada3ae250e9989584adb7f4b89c5f701d60.jpg)

# Checking steps

CAUTION:

Do not overpressurize the lower unit. Excessive pressure may damage the oil seals.

(1) Remove the gear oil level check screw. (2) Install the pressure tester into the check hole.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Pressure tester YB-35956 / 90890-06762</td></tr></table>

(3) Apply the specified pressure.

NOTE:

The lower unit should hold the specified pressure for 10 seconds.

# GENERAL CHECKING THE ANODES

Check:

• Anodes $\textcircled{1}$   
• Trim tab $\textcircled{2}$ Scales Clean. $\mathsf { G r e a s e / o i l } \to \mathsf { C l e a n }$ . Excessive wear Replace.

# CAUTION:

Do not oil, grease or paint the anode, or it will not operate properly.

# CHECKING THE BATTERY

# WARNING

Battery electrolytic fluid is dangerous; it contains sulfuric acid and therefore is poisonous and highly caustic.

Always follow these preventive measures:

• Avoid bodily contact with electrolytic fluid as it can cause severe burns or permanent eye injury.

• Wear protective eye gear when handling or working near batteries.

Antidote (EXTERNAL):

• SKIN - Flush with water.

• EYES - Flush with water for 15 minutes and get immediate medical attention.

Antidote (INTERNAL):

• Drink large quantities of water or milk followed by milk of magnesia, beaten egg, or vegetable oil. Get immediate medical attention.

Batteries also generate explosive hydrogen gas; therefore, you should always follow these preventive measures:

• Charge batteries in a well-ventilated area.   
• Keep batteries away from fire, sparks, or open flames (e.g., welding equipment, lighted cigarettes, etc.).   
• DO NOT SMOKE when charging or handling batteries.

KEEP BATTERIES AND ELECTROLYTIC FLUID OUT OF REACH OF CHILDREN.

# NOTE:

• Batteries vary among manufacturers. Therefore, the following procedures may not always apply. Consult your battery manufacturer’s instructions. • First, disconnect the negative lead, then the positive lead.

# Check:

• Electrolyte level Below the minimum level mark Add distilled water to the proper level.   
• Electrolyte specific gravity Less than specification Recharge the battery.

![](images/0293e1af64a9485583adb9c29431356894b6df85789882354dd59ef18420672c.jpg)

![](images/fc3b50b11243b25de3fd7714e7e352cfee628d125d6a0fe09da862642d43dea0.jpg)

# CHECKING THE SPARK PLUGS

1. Check:

• Electrodes $\textcircled{1}$ Cracks/excessive wear Replace.   
• Insulator color $\textcircled{2}$ Distinctly different color Check the engine condition.

2. Clean: • Spark plug (with a spark plug cleaner or wire brush.)

![](images/f4e6eb160733c47d6de32647bf4c619af922bcf39fc5dc638825447a1369add0.jpg)

3. Measure:

• Spark plug gap $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Regap.

Spark plug gap 1.0 - 1.1 mm (0.039 - 0.043 in)

![](images/9bb5d70855204998489f824c5dab8594f5b1018e58b52b013799a942fa3f0cc5.jpg)

4. Tighten: • Spark plug

<table><tr><td></td><td>Spark plug 25 Nm (2.5 m · kgf, 18 ft · Ib)</td></tr></table>

# NOTE:

• Before installing the spark plug, clean the gasket surface and spark plug surface. Also, it is suggested to apply a thin film of anti-seize compound to the spark plug threads to prevent thread seizure. • If a torque wrench is not available, a good estimate of the correct tightening torque is to finger tighten $\textcircled{2}$ the spark plug and then tighten it another $1 / 4$ to $\boldsymbol { \mathsf { 1 / 2 } }$ of a turn $\textcircled{6}$ .

# COMPRESSION PRESSURE MEASUREMENT

# CAUTION:

Before removing a spark plug, use compressed air to blow away dirt accumulated in the spark plug well to prevent it from falling into the cylinder that is being tested.

1. Check:

• Valve clearance Out of specification Adjust. Refer to “ADJUSTING THE VALVE CLEARANCE” on page 3-13.

2. Warm-up: • Engine

3. Remove: • Spark plug(-s)

![](images/9934aebde5f780983df234299053ed8901d68fa2ce23e8c99ab9bfdb97d8ce53.jpg)

4. Install: • Compression gauge $\textcircled{1}$ (into the spark plug hole)

NOTE:   
Use a compression gauge that is used for automobiles.

5. Measure:

• Compression pressure   
Below minimum compression pres  
sure Inspect valve clearance, valve   
face, valve seat, piston rings, cylinder sleeve, piston, cylinder head gasket and cylinder head.

Compression pressure Minimum 950 kPa (9.5 kg/cm2, 135 psi)

# Measurement steps

(1) Remove the lock plate from the engine stop lanyard switch on the remote control box.

(2) With the throttle wide open, crank the engine setting the main switch in the START position until the reading on the compression gauge stabilizes.

6. Remove: • Compression gauge

7. Install: • Spark plug(-s)

![](images/7ad65914c0df2c81d2e12d95bb4e2b29dd45e2cdbe299257e9f4a8e90ede7b46.jpg)

# REDUCING THE FUEL PRESSURE(HIGH-PRESSURE FUEL LINE)

# WARNING

Always reduce the fuel pressure in the high-pressure fuel line before servicing the line or the vapor separator. If the fuel pressure is not released, pressurized fuel may spray out.

1. Reduce: • Fuel pressure (high-pressure fuel line)

# Reducing steps

(1) Install the fuel pressure gauge onto the pressure check valve.

# Fuel pressure gauge.. 1 YB-06766 / 90890-06786

(2) Place the drain hose into a container. (3) Open the valve $\textcircled{2}$ and release the pressure.

2. Drain: • Fuel

![](images/69afe4070d0cdd0a1201424c96474816d56c05f65b10bc9f003dea10a3a70268.jpg)

# CHECKING THE PRESSUREREGULATOR

Check: • Pressure regulator Faulty Replace the pressure regulator.

# Checking steps

(1) Install the fuel pressure gauge onto the pressure check valve.

![](images/8d9183bfa240ae5e1fd56b1c5927ffa806c4daf58774237a3ffa30ebc1addc0d.jpg)

(2) Main switch to on.   
(3) Check the fuel pressure.

![](images/6188b43996345d6c9e7193287d44ac2cae91d62ba3cdb83cb307ae29a7127dc7.jpg)

Fuel pressure Approx. 300 kPa (3.0 kg/cm2, 44.1 psi)

(4) Start the engine.   
(5) Check the fuel pressure. Fuel pressure   
Approx.   
250 kPa (2.5 kg/cm2, 35.6 psi)

![](images/e7b1bb831d2ca15e2f2127ca9bc7b6307181cf42796c622b50806e1b1106b7b2.jpg)

![](images/403266eeea8f50cb376feeae39b59218251737fe21676e5d2dd77e315c730f5e.jpg)

# CHECKING THE FUEL PUMPS

1. Check: • Diaphragm • Fuel pump valves Damage Replace.

2. Check: • Fuel pump Reverse air flow Replace.

![](images/632bbc32cf4b6333c47e90e15d10a44f604e7a233c99aec2dc94d601934c9229.jpg)

# Checking steps

NOTE:   
Do not overpressurize the fuel pump. Excessive pressure may cause air to leak out.

(1) Install the Mity vac onto the fuel pump as shown.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Mity vac</td></tr><tr><td>22288</td><td>YB-35956 / 90890-06756</td></tr></table>

(2) Apply the specified pressure with the Mity vac.

Fuel pump pressure $\textcircled{2}$ 50 kPa (0.5 kg/cm2, 7.1 psi) Fuel pump negative pressure $\textcircled{6}$ 30 kPa (0.3 kg/cm2, 4.3 psi)

![](images/5023a4b623ab36ce95b812520439244b6184601428f9babfcbeaa7b1b7d562a9.jpg)

# NOTE:

• Make sure no air comes out of the opposite side of the fuel pump.   
• To eliminate any gaps between the fuel pump valves and the fuel pump body, and to ensure a better seal, make sure the inside of the fuel pump is wet (i.e., with   
gas).

# REMOVING THE FLYWHEEL MAGNET ASSEMBLY

1. Remove: • Flywheel magnet assembly nut

![](images/5bd9014f861f3a51ff3b925313b01c417809932f3f3adbd64018d76f7519fc69.jpg)

Flywheel magnet assembly holder YB-06139 / 90890-06522

Å For USA and Canada ı For worldwide

2. Remove: • Flywheel magnet assembly

<table><tr><td>bs</td><td>Universal puller YB-06117 / 90890-06521</td></tr></table>

Å For USA and Canada ı For worldwide

# CAUTION:

• Keep the nut side flush with the crankshaft end until the flywheel magnet assembly comes off the tapered portion of the crankshaft.   
• To prevent damage to the engine or tools, screw in the universal-puller setbolts evenly and completely so that the universal-puller plate is parallel to the flywheel magnet assembly.

# INSTALLING THE TIMING BELT

# CAUTION:

• Never forcefully twist, turn inside out, or bend the timing belt.   
• Do not let oil or grease get onto the timing belt.

• $\textcircled{6}$ Minimum 25 mm (1.0 in)

Install:

• Timing belt • Tensioner

# Installation steps

(1) Align ø6 hole on the pickup rotor with the notch in the cylinder block.   
(2) Align the marks $" \bigtriangledown \cdot \mathbf { \omega }$ on the driven sprockets with the top edge of the cylinder head.   
(3) Install the timing belt onto the driven sprockets and drive sprocket.

(4) Install the tensioner.

# Tensioner bolt 40 Nm (4.0 m • kgf, 29 ft • lb)

(5) Turn the crankshaft clockwise two times and make sure the drive sprocket and driven sprockets are correctly aligned with the marks.

# CHECKING THE CAMSHAFT

1. Measure: • Camshaft lobe dimensions $\textcircled{2}$ and $\textcircled{6}$ Out of specification Replace the camshaft.

![](images/51e296fe07eab4631262792a9109ab49605e90a4df15af929da8f84d847469c7.jpg)

# Camshaft lobe dimension

$\textcircled{2}$ IN: 37.22 - 37.38 mm (1.465 - 1.472 in)   
$\textcircled{6}$ IN: 29.92 - 30.08 mm (1.178 - 1.184 in)   
$\textcircled{2}$ EX: 36.90 - 37.06 mm (1.453 - 1.459 in)   
b EX: 29.92 - 30.08 mm (1.178 - 1.184 in)

![](images/c104794981961bc896c4edb0a49cf4be251959f90f0b61effc755197aed472e0.jpg)

![](images/9ff466b3f007c9e5de304e144bd4eaab9a54c134cb58a66b28a25816bd37f521.jpg)

2. Measure:

• Camshaft journal diameter $\textcircled{2}$ • Camshaft cap inside diameter $\textcircled{6}$ Out of specification Replace the camshaft or cylinder head.

![](images/e0e47da78f056d707b6ba0886c1c61ad37d76334fccd3980aaa41305bb1b487e.jpg)

Camshaft journal diameter a: 24.96 - 24.98 mm (0.9827 - 0.9835 in)   
Camshaft cap inside diameter b: 25.000 - 25.021 mm (0.984 - 0.985 in)

# INSTALLING THE CAMSHAFT

Install:

• Camshaft • Camshaft cap

# Installation steps

(1) Before installing the exhaust and intake camshafts, turn the crankshaft until cylinder #1’s piston is at TDC on the compression stroke.   
(2) Install the camshaft caps in the proper position as shown and with the stamped numbers facing upside down.

# CHECKING THE THERMOSTAT

Check:   
• Thermostat Damage/valve does not open Replace.

2. Measure: • Valve operating temperature • Valve lift $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Replace the thermostat.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>公</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Water temperature</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Valve lift</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Below50℃ (122°F)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0 mm (0 in)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Above60℃ (140°F)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Min. 4.3 mm(0.17 in)</td></tr></table>

# Measuring steps

(1) Suspend the thermostat in a container filled with water.   
(2) Slowly heat the water.   
(3) Place a thermometer in the water.   
(4) While stirring the water, observe the thermometer’s indicated temperature.

![](images/1eecb277467b5bef6e8eb177dc8ea2f5c6031838ff0032c2a59b2cf536aee1e0.jpg)

# CHECKING THE VALVE

. Check:   
• Valve Damage/warpage Replace.

2. Measure: • Margin thickness $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Replace.

![](images/68f34b153408e0e4f4e6c3b39cc93786a82fe12915e7ba1f745d78ef77e313a1.jpg)

Margin thickness IN: 0.8 - 1.2 mm (0.031 - 0.047 in) EX: 1.0 - 1.4 mm (0.039 - 0.055 in)

![](images/36a92f712c2a4fafdeb4e4cf7bb62658217654fb53252978f7f9c06fd017d626.jpg)

![](images/97b049300b6e0a618290b77e75c8679269a53234d51604b71455fb38b81e4967.jpg)

3. Measure:

• Valve stem diameter $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Replace.

![](images/b68e8ccd5a37a48a582944a53fccf69ba6b5c9a92cb21852795e2f893d606794.jpg)

Valve stem diameter IN: 5.975 - 5.990 mm (0.2352 - 0.2358 in) EX: 5.960 - 5.975 mm (0.2346 - 0.2352 in)

4. Measure: • Valve stem runout Out of specification Replace.

![](images/cb12d3f4bb2c4a901347512f80cda2edf35b569f160d913a027506c623319955.jpg)

Valve stem runout limit IN and EX 0.03 mm (0.001 in)

NOTE:

The valve guide, valve seal, and valve should be replaced as a set.

1. Measure: • Free length $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Replace.

# CHECKING THE CYLINDER HEAD

Measure:

• Cylinder head warpage Out of specification Reface or replace.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Warpage limit 0.1 mm (0.004 in)</td></tr></table>

# CHECKING THE VALVE GUIDE

Measure:

• Valve guide bore $\textcircled{2}$   
Out of specification Replace the guide.

![](images/a67105880409f1761853d6a3a875a5fb25bf40248e6de144ec021efb06a1085a.jpg)

Valve guide bore 6.005 - 6.018 mm (0.2364 - 0.2369 in)

# Replacement steps

(1) Remove the valve guide with the valve guide remover/installer.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Valve guide remover</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>YM-4064-A / 90890-04064</td></tr></table>

![](images/394afced8958232814029d4ad36f96fe799e1cb42cf37468a6e271d5e6e963c4.jpg)

![](images/b315825b44e160d75734a97e5f07f51daf2995e6492d5914e9726acb107b49d9.jpg)

(2) Install the new valve guide to the specified position (from the top of the valve guide bore as shown) $\textcircled{2}$ with the valve guide remover/installer.

![](images/697d35911d79fba770056d5956e24c4b6635999d31be37f7f2c3707cc2e80713.jpg)

# Valve guide position 11.5 mm (0.45 in)

(3) After installing the valve guide, bore the valve guide with the valve guide reamer.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Valve guide reamer YM-04066 / 90890-04066</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

• Heat the cylinder head in an oven to $\mathsf { 2 0 0 ^ { \circ } C }$ $( 3 9 2 ^ { \circ } \mathsf { F } )$ to ease valve guide removal and installation, and to maintain the correct interference fit. • Before installing the valve guide, mark its installation position $\textcircled{6}$ as shown.

![](images/76c501ef39fa8108c7a0db11bcfeb3d32fec74813de08c52a1f0ca53cee42702.jpg)

![](images/fbd7bd38491093c47b6f8f1ace1872421ce565a0fd3444f0fdd1eee63176eb24.jpg)

# CHECKING THE VALVE SEAT

1. Measure: • Valve seat width $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Reface the valve seat.

Valve seat width Intake 1.58 - 1.94 mm (0.062 - 0.076 in) Exhaust 1.80 - 2.02 mm (0.071 - 0.080 in)

2. Reface: • Valve seat

# CAUTION:

To prevent chatter marks, turn the valve seat cutter while an even, downward pressure $( 4 - 5 \ k g )$ .

![](images/789996bf528ddf41610675fd81d64e96dfcf045778861487a123621b8da73df0.jpg)

Valve seat cutter set YM-91043-C / 90890-06803 Valve seat cutter holder YB-06553 / 90890-06553 Valve seat cutter (45˚) YB-06555 / 90890-06555 (90˚) YB-06556 / 90890-06556 • Refer to the following chart to determine the appropriate valve seat cutter.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Valve seat area</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Valve seat cutter</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>A</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>90°</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>B</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>45$</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

After refacing the valve seat or replacing the valve and valve guide, lap the valve seat and valve face.

![](images/0ecfd18c6cf4c1fef8676e0c87c260575a143c1eef0f69783563fa3d13f0f9bf.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE VALVE

1. Install:

• Valve stem seal $\textcircled{1}$ • Valve $\textcircled{2}$ • Spring seat $\textcircled{3}$ • Valve spring $\textcircled{4}$ • Spring retainer $\textcircled{5}$

2. Install: • Valve cotter $\textcircled{6}$

<table><tr><td></td><td>Valve spring compressor YM-01253 / 90890-04019 Valve spring compressor adapter YB-06554 / 90890-06554</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

Compress the valve spring with the special tools and install the cotters onto the valve.

# OIL FILTER AND EXHAUST COVERREMOVING/INSTALLING THE OIL FILTER AND EXHAUST COVER

![](images/85ac7dbb1d4d2eaecc7640d3e2c0e3c893faf3179836ca560862643154153b9d.jpg)

# CHECKING THE CYLINDER BLOCK

Measure:

• Cylinder bore Out of specification Rebore the cylinder or replace the cylinder block.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>公</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Standard</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Wearlimit</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Cylinderbore &quot;D&quot;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>79.000 - 79.020 mm(3.110 - 3.111 in)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Taper limit&quot;T&quot;</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08 mm(0.003 in)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Out ofround limit</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08 mm(0.003 in)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=4>D = Maximum Dia. (D1 - D6)T = (maximum D1 or D2) - (minimum D5or D6)</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

Measure the cylinder bore in parallel and at a right angle to the crankshaft. Then, average the measurements.

![](images/9c5809b66609ad1c0aed77db6f77decdb9431fedf9c012d56edc955db4780727.jpg)

• Piston diameter

# CALCULATING THE PISTON-TOCYLINDER CLEARANCE

Calculate:

• Piston-to-cylinder clearance Out of specification Replace the piston and piston rings, the cylinder block or both.

# CHECKING THE PISTON RING

1. Measure:   
• End gap $\textcircled{2}$ Out of specification Replace the piston rings as a set.

![](images/2215f1db0c396678b2920b91c1cc321728c6a13288fba0efe8f09ece45ffc884.jpg)

End gap (installed) Top ring 0.15 - 0.30 mm (0.006 - 0.012 in) 2nd ring 0.70 - 0.90 mm (0.028 - 0.035 in) Oil ring 0.20 - 0.70 mm (0.008 - 0.028 in)

NOTE:

Push the piston ring into the cylinder with the piston crown.

# CHECKING THE MAIN-BEARING OIL CLEARANCE

1. Measure: • Main-bearing oil clearance Out of specification Replace the upper and lower bearings as a set.

![](images/7420977509d27c939fde7021164787ee007304c487b58c3a00cae3726017b585.jpg)

NOTE:

Measure the main-bearing oil clearance at room temperature $( 2 0 ~ \textdegree C$ (68 ˚F)).

# CRANKSHAFT AND PISTON/ POWR CONNECTING ROD ASSEMBLY

![](images/8444aef3d5efb6fe19e8bbbefde480e4d6a66e0530e43b5d034c12b871f73279.jpg)

![](images/0218981236933cd3fd51e43036814e4e5a0d831682ad0da6b51ff344388c3870.jpg)

![](images/486ce2a5b687c6ba21e1ef8f74d605b18b10df3b804f277b3a017818f470f1b6.jpg)

![](images/50a2b7449a97970f1c755d5ba0dd2201a139be2df3ad04ec65e2d0bf2a0ee58e.jpg)

# Measuring steps

# CAUTION:

Install the bearings in their original positions. Incorrect oil clearance measurements can lead to engine damage.

(1) Clean the bearings, main journals, and bearing portions of the crankcase and cylinder block.   
(2) Place the cylinder block upside down on a bench.   
(3) Install half of the bearings $\textcircled{1}$ and the crankshaft $\textcircled{2}$ into the cylinder block $\textcircled{3}$ .   
(4) Put a piece of Plastigauge on each main journal in parallel to the crankshaft.

# NOTE:

Do not put the Plastigauge over the oil hole in the main journal of the crankshaft.

(5) Install the other half of the bearings into the crankcase.   
(6) Install the crankcase onto the cylinder block.   
(7) Apply engine oil on to the threads and seat of the crankcase bolts.   
(8) Tighten the bolts to the specified torque in two steps in the order shown in the illustration.

# NOTE:

Do not move the crankshaft until the mainbearing oil clearance measurement has been completed.

Bolt (M8) 1st: 14 Nm (1.4 m • kgf, 10 ft • lb) 2nd: 28 Nm (2.8 m • kgf, 20 ft • lb)   
Bolt (M10) 1st: 19 Nm (1.9 m • kgf, 14 ft • lb) 2nd: 60˚ 50 Nm (5.0 m • kgf, 36 ft • lb)\*

(9) Remove the crankcase. (10) Measure the width of the compressed Plastigauge on each main journal.

\* Torque valve (for reference only)

# CRANKSHAFT AND PISTON/ CONNECTING ROD ASSEMBLY

![](images/8dacb87e4bcc7bb9250a9694c8b9d7d0d0549f84c32466bd12b777d4f2692b47.jpg)

![](images/907a1df98a38cb36e95ddbf0c86b7b52121ce50f5cc382306e3783044daf737d.jpg)

![](images/da846c19f847a703abdc4122a643404fc624195c0b1107a46d94c76c40cc306f.jpg)

2. Adjust: • Main-bearing oil clearance

NOTE:

Adjust the main-bearing oil clearance at room temperature $\iota 2 0 ^ { \circ } \mathsf C$ (68 ˚F)).

# Adjusting steps

# CAUTION:

Remove any oil or dust from the cylinder block and crankcase bearing mounting surfaces.

# NOTE:

The cylinder block journal diameters (#1 - #5) and the crankshaft journal diameters, (#1 - #5) can be determined by the stamped value as described below.

Crankshaft journal diameter $= 4 7 . 9 0 0 +$   
(stamped value/1000)   
Example: # $1 = 9 2 \to 4 7 . 9 9 2$   
Cylinder block journal diameter $= 5 4 . 0 0 0 \ + $   
(stamped value/1000)   
Example: # $\mid = 3 2  5 4 . 0 3 2$   
(1) Subtract the crankshaft journal diameters (#1 - #5) from the cylinder block journal diameters (#1 - #5).   
(2) Select the suitable bearing from the table below according to the calculated values.

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=3>Crankshaft bearing selection table(20℃ (68F))</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Cylinder blockjournal diameters -crankshaft journaldiameters(mm)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Bearing(cylinder side)/thrust bearing</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Bearing(crankcaseside)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>6.023 - 6.0266.027 - 6.0346.035 - 6.0426.043 - 6.0496.050 - 6.058</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>GreenBlueBlueRedRed</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Yellow*Green*BlueBlue*Red</td></tr></table>

# CAUTION:

The $( ^ { \ast } )$ mark indicates that the color of the upper and lower bearings are different. Install the main-bearings in the middle of the cylinder block and crankcase journal so they do not block the oil holes.

# NOTE:

Crankshaft bearing #3 is a thrust bearing.

(3) If the difference between the cylinder block journal diameter and crankshaft journal diameter is more than the maximum value $( 6 . 0 5 8 ~ \mathsf { m m } )$ , replace the crankshaft, cylinder block, or both.

# CHECKING THE CONNECTING ROD BIG-END OIL CLEARANCE

# CAUTION:

• Mark the original connecting rod bolts so they are not confused with the new bolts. • Do not reuse the original connecting rod bolts during assembly, only use them when measuring and adjusting the oil clearance. • Before assembly, remove any small metal particles from the big- end mating surface and also thoroughly clean it.

# 1. Measure:

• Big-end oil clearance Out of specification Replace the upper and lower bearings as a set.

![](images/17cf2cf1af5ae395defecc2703cf8e5aa3529160bdf51e3542415f1be6eb1939.jpg)

Big-end oil clearance 0.025 - 0.031 mm (0.0010 - 0.0012 in)

NOTE:

Measure the big-end oil clearance at room temperature $\left( 2 0 ^ { \circ } { \bf C } ( 6 8 ^ { \circ } { \bf F } ) \right)$ ).

![](images/7f161b5de8a7ad6b4f11541666a12dca1e18518b5f1821070b065ca6c3a2bcf7.jpg)

![](images/dc01776534b5bda18957ce3465881862615e816f091ee295ee54a59474887c1d.jpg)

# Measuring steps

# CAUTION:

Install the bearings in their original positions. Incorrect oil clearance measurements can lead to engine damage.

(1) Clean the bearings and bearing portions of the connecting rod.   
(2) Install the upper half of the bearing into the connecting rod and the lower half into the connecting rod cap.   
(3) Put a piece of Plastigauge onto the crank pin in parallel to the crankshaft.   
(4) Assemble the connecting rod onto the crank pin.

# NOTE:

• Make sure the projections $\textcircled{2}$ and “YAMAHA” mark on the connecting rod faces towards the flywheel side. • Do not move the crankshaft until the bigend oil clearance measurement has been completed.

(5) Apply engine oil onto the threads and seat of the original connecting rod bolts.   
(6) Tighten the original bolts to the specified torque in two stages.

![](images/77374f189de29d5d11bf1723cf58f8d97320f6afb5961d9eef1eb52a9c6744d4.jpg)

# Bolt

![](images/8ac234e5c79f9cb3e4607c4298a7aa978cac5ab2acf99330c41dfc09b55b43da.jpg)

1st: 15 Nm (1.5 m $\bullet$ kgf, 11 ft • lb)   
2nd: 60˚

(7) Remove the connecting rod cap. (8) Measure the width of the compressed Plastigauge on each crank pin.

# CRANKSHAFT AND PISTON/ CONNECTING ROD ASSEMBLY

2. Adjust: • Big-end oil clearance

# NOTE:

![](images/e63bf9e42587f3127e1be48d77b27d6fa100dd06973b34f43b1a5204df63e5be.jpg)

![](images/47475d352a17d06af3643eb34fcb8a9880f47145aa7ee64ce12cb6d793cf860a.jpg)

![](images/ffb5e2d0c27c8d80e3a39fec592fe469e9af06907304107ccd392177c2458c42.jpg)

Adjust the big-end oil clearance at room temperature $\left( 2 0 ^ { \circ } { \bf C } ( 6 8 ^ { \circ } { \bf F } ) \right.$ ).

# Adjusting steps

# CAUTION:

# Remove any oil or dust from the connecting-rod-bearing mounting surfaces.

(1) Install the new yellow bearings into the connecting rods and connecting rod caps.   
(2) Put a piece of Plastigauge onto the crank pin in parallel to the crankshaft.   
(3) Assemble the connecting rod onto the crank pin.

# NOTE:

• Make sure the projections $\textcircled{2}$ and “YAMAHA” mark on the connecting rod faces towards the flywheel side. • Do not move the crankshaft until the bigend oil clearance measurement has been completed.

(4) Apply engine oil onto the threads and seat of the original connecting rod bolts.   
(5) Tighten the original bolts to the specified torque in two stages.

# Bolt

![](images/0da66a47ba3a459929dfd77463e36352f6a22d6e924f8dcd0b67e6d77d7011f4.jpg)

1st: 15 Nm (1.5 m • kgf, 11 ft • lb)   
2nd: 60˚

(6) Remove the connecting rod cap. (7) Measure the width of the compressed Plastigauge on each crank pin. (8) Select the suitable bearing from the table below according to the measurement values.

# CRANKSHAFT AND PISTON/ CONNECTING ROD ASSEMBLY

# CAUTION:

# The $( ^ { \ast } )$ mark indicates that the color of the upper and lower bearings are different.

(9) If the measurement value is more than the maximum value $( 0 . 0 7 1 \quad \mathrm { ~ m m } )$ , replace the crankshaft, connecting rod, or both.

![](images/83485eb5cba7aa38a19b2c7a7396133e79d346072855fe4604a0922985af47a3.jpg)

# REMOVING THE PROPELLER

Remove: • Propeller

# WARNING

Do not hold the propeller with your hands when removing or installing it. Be sure to remove the battery leads from the batteries and the lanyard engine stop switch. Put a block of wood between the cavitation plate and propeller to keep the propeller from turning.

# CHECKING THE PROPELLER

Check:

• Blades   
• Splines Cracks/damage/wear Replace.

![](images/80b92cee0def78aa7250772a9d80b06cbb952836aadbc6b6c74e38c578b85d9f.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE PROPELLER

nstall: • Propeller

# WARNING

Do not hold the propeller with your hands when removing or installing it. Be sure to remove the battery leads from the batteries and the lanyard engine stop switch. Put a block of wood between the cavitation plate and propeller to keep the propeller from turning.

# NOTE:

If the groove in the propeller nut is not aligned with the cotter pin hole, tighten the nut further until they are aligned.

# INSTALLING THE IMPELLER ANDIMPELLER HOUSING

1. Install: • Washers $\textcircled{1}$ • Wave washer $\textcircled{2}$ • Spacer $\textcircled{3}$ • Collar 4

NOTE:

• The collar and spacer should fit together firmly. • While pulling the drive shaft up, install the collar with some appropriate tool $\textcircled{2}$ that fits over the drive shaft as shown.

# 2. Install:

• O-ring $\textcircled{1}$   
• Impeller housing cup $\textcircled{2}$   
• Impeller housing $\textcircled{3}$   
• O-ring $\textcircled{4}$

# NOTE:

• When installing the impeller housing cup, align its projection with the hole in the impeller housing. • When installing the water pump housing, turn the drive shaft clockwise.

# REMOVING THE PROPELLER

Remove: • Propeller

# WARNING

Do not hold the propeller with your hands when removing or installing it. Be sure to remove the battery leads from the batteries and the lanyard engine stop switch. Put a block of wood between the cavitation plate and propeller to keep the propeller from turning.

# CHECKING THE PROPELLER

Check:

• Blades   
• Splines Cracks/damage/wear Replace.

![](images/ac2b787c25e4313cca0ab7c4ec38fa09fc16dd1805f25488c0cc94a22c3b9676.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE PROPELLER

nstall: • Propeller

# WARNING

Do not hold the propeller with your hands when removing or installing it. Be sure to remove the battery leads from the batteries and the lanyard engine stop switch. Put a block of wood between the cavitation plate and propeller to keep the propeller from turning.

# NOTE:

If the groove in the propeller nut is not aligned with the cotter pin hole, tighten the nut further until they are aligned.

# SHIMMING (REGULAR ROTATION MODELS) (FOR USA AND CANADA)

# NOTE:

• There is no need to select shims when reassembling with the original case and inner parts. • Shim calculations are required when reassembling with the original inner parts and a new case (the difference between the original inner parts and the new case). • Measurements and adjustments are required when replacing the inner part(s).

![](images/0218f7d6edcf486a3d5adc00ceba0bc57f5524a1da9ec746319650d75fb0904f.jpg)

![](images/2898dbbdc75394f051895d007d1dd461af4a1ecfbe0d77e3f38c9745301dd482.jpg)

![](images/61bc5459cc1d78483bc1c2292d0773e30520a3dcf37ccd64ee6f687f737d3e2c.jpg)

![](images/0a1eb31a403d8c4eeb2377c4d97aa475543d867126fcc2502a173841decab830.jpg)

# SELECTING THE PINION SHIMS

# NOTE:

Find the shim thickness (T3) by selecting shims until the specified value (M0) is obtained with the special tool.

1. Measure: • Specified measurement (M) Out of specified value $( \mathsf { M } 0 ) \to \mathsf { A d j }$ ust.

# Specified value (M0) = 1.00 + P/100 mm

# Measuring steps

(1) Calculate the specified value (M0).

# NOTE:

“P” is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

Example:   
If $" { \sf P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\yen 50$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 0 0 + ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ = 1.00 + 0.05 mm = 1.05 mm   
If $" { \sf P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 3 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 0 0 + ( - 3 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ $= 1 . 0 0 - 0 . 0 3 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 9 7 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

<table><tr><td>LOWR</td><td></td></tr></table>

![](images/5339ee1a1ca23781be320f93339de2d3883779d54830880916b7f75ea186c74c.jpg)

(2) Install the pinion height gauge, drive shaft, thrust bearing $\textcircled{1}$ , and shim(s) $\textcircled{2}$ .

<table><tr><td></td><td>Pinion height gauge</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>YB-34432-6, -11</td></tr></table>

NOTE:

If the original shim(s) is unavailable, start with a 0.50-mm shim.

(3) Install the pinion and pinion nut.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Pinion nut 93 Nm (9.3 m · kgf, 67 ft · Ib)</td></tr></table>

![](images/401751f6bd0bf11465f0671e2ad4375b1704992af4c2ec860f4b74557d1e8827.jpg)

(4) Measure the specified measurement(M).

# NOTE:

• Measure the clearance between the pinion height gauge and the lower surface of the pinion as shown.   
• Perform the same measurement at three points on the pinion.   
• Find the average of the measurements (M).

2. Adjust: • Shim thickness (T3) Remove or add shim(s).

![](images/3160ccf1bf33e86da9c04851109f34b3e77f89a907c8bbc9613c7100517efbc0.jpg)

Available shim thickness 0.10, 0.12, 0.15, 0.18, 0.30, 0.40 and 0.50 mm

(M0) – (M) should be as close to $" 0 "$ as possible.

![](images/0f2e54b46aee6f005959ed8d6e16460e844366d387201760e3e3da66ba336cd7.jpg)

# Specified value (M0) = 1.80 + F/100 mm

# Measuring steps

(1) Calculate the specified value (M0).

# NOTE:

“F” is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - } \mathsf { m m }$ units. If the $" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume an “F” value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

Example:   
If “F” is $\yen 50$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 8 0 + ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ = 1.80 + 0.05 mm = 1.85 mm   
If $" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 3 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 8 0 + ( - 3 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ $= 1 . 8 0 - 0 . 0 3 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 1 . 7 7 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

![](images/5861ff422a16f35b6a773090839be064a995fff800a9f4ef282fa6920b4ee8f0.jpg)

(2) Install the shimming gauge, bearing $\textcircled{1} .$ , and shim(s) $\textcircled{2}$ .

NOTE:

If the original shim(s) is unavailable, start with a 0.50-mm shim.

# SELECTING THE REVERSE GEAR SHIMS

# NOTE:

Find the shim thickness (T2) by selecting shims until the specified value (M0) is obtained with the special tool.

1. Measure: • Specified measurement (M) Out of specified value $( \mathsf { M } 0 ) \to \mathsf { A d j }$ ust.

![](images/fd680eaf03e3d7b3bb4b672db6406a22fcbee4cbe65f68e7b92b8f795b6c0372.jpg)

# Specified value (M0) = 1.80 – R/100 mm

# Measuring steps

(1) Calculate the specified value (M0).

# NOTE:

$\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume an $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

Example:   
If $\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\mathit { \Pi } ^ { \prime \prime } { + } 5 \mathit { \Pi } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 8 0 - ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ = 1.80 – 0.05 mm = 1.75 mm   
If $\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 3 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 8 0 - ( - 3 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ $= 1 . 8 0 + 0 . 0 3 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 1 . 8 3 ~ \mathsf { m m }$

![](images/e64ed6e11237b6ef1de913d3e33e83ce3f7af477ad97a0de67f8380f75fceb33.jpg)

(2) Install the shimming gauge, bearing, thrust washer, reverse gear, and shim(s).

<table><tr><td></td><td>Shimming gauge YB-34468-2</td></tr></table>

# NOTE:

• If the original shim(s) is unavailable, start with a $0 . 5 0 – \mathsf { m m }$ shim.   
• Turn the reverse gear assembly a few times until the gear and bearing are horizontal.

(3) Measure the specified measurement (M).

2. Adjust: • Shim thickness (T2) Remove or add shim(s).

![](images/b7fe3bc5f5e974c447d6633bd23470c7f15d7bace9c11204eb34b381351aec6c.jpg)

Available shim thickness 0.10, 0.12, 0.15, 0.18, 0.30, 0.40 and 0.50 mm

NOTE:   
(M0) – (M) should be as close to $" 0 "$ as possible.

NOTE:

(2) Install the pinion and pinion nut.

<table><tr><td>R</td><td>Pinion nut 93 Nm (9.3 m · kgf, 67 ft · Ib)</td></tr></table>

(3) Install the pinion height gauge.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Pinion height gauge 90890-06702</td></tr></table>

# NOTE:

After the wing nuts contact the fixing plate, tighten them another $1 / 4$ of a turn.

(4) Measure (M4).

<table><tr><td>8008</td><td>Digital caliper 90890-06704</td></tr></table>

# NOTE:

# SHIMMING (REGULAR ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

![](images/909d89c798d251880f8ee6c146a6270dac80a0057717bfc9ce50400efcd1cdd0.jpg)

(5) Calculate the pinion shim thickness (T3).

Pinion shim thickness (T3) = 62.5 + P/100 – M3 – M4

# NOTE:

“P” is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# Example:

If M3 is $^ { \prime \prime } 4 6 . 8 5 \mathrm { \ m m ^ { \prime \prime } }$ , M4 is $^ { \prime \prime } 1 5 . 1 2 \mathsf { m m } ^ { \prime \prime }$ and   
P is $\mathtt { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 5 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
T3 = 62.5 + (–5)/100 – 46.85 – 15.12 mm $= 6 2 . 5 - 0 . 0 5 - 4 6 . 8 5 - 1 5 . 1 2 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 4 8 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(6) Select the pinion shim(s) (T3).

# SELECTING THE FORWARD GEAR SHIMS

# NOTE:

Select the shim thickness (T1) by using the specified measurement(s) and the calculation formula.

Select: • Shim thickness (T1)

Selecting steps (1) Measure (M1).

![](images/ffbef5680446eb53e8f193d6d139406aae86478690703cdb9c0e5469cb5e2343.jpg)

# NOTE:

• Turn the roller bearing outer race two or three times so the rollers seat. Then, measure the height of the bearing, as shown. • Perform the same measurement at three points on the roller bearing outer race. • Find the average of the measurements (M1).

![](images/e2df2f3cd768f7f656fcb729b2ae5aacdced777df79f7236251c9f7f6d68be2d.jpg)

(2) Calculate the forward gear shim thickness (T1).

![](images/a5ddd4543eca44a9b0c620278ce0705383d28caf3b10de91659768c240e82557.jpg)

# Forward gear shim thickness (T1) (T1) = 24.6 + F/100 – M1

# NOTE:

$" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - } \mathsf { m m }$ units. If the $" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume an “F” value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# SHIMMING (REGULAR ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

Example:

If M1 is $^ { \prime \prime } 2 4 . 1 0 \mathsf { m m } ^ { \prime \prime }$ and F is $\prime 5 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { T } 1 = 2 4 . 6 + ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 - 2 4 . 1 0 \mathsf { m m }$ $= 2 4 . 6 + 0 . 0 5 - 2 4 . 1 0 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 5 5 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(3) Select the forward gear shim(s) (T1).

![](images/de860646ad5f1c9b2b25bda678cbcd55b0b256793043a849b2197ecfe232ba60.jpg)

# NOTE:

• Measure the height of the gear as shown.

# SHIMMING (REGULAR ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

(2) Calculate the reverse gear shim thickness (T2).

![](images/e91788d14ed1062184844d154dcb52e7a5ea184e2ada5751c84c333053ad003c.jpg)

Reverse gear shim thickness (T2) = M2 – 27.4 – R/100

# NOTE:

$\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# Example:

If M2 is $^ { \prime \prime } 2 7 . 9 5 \mathrm { \ m m ^ { \prime \prime } }$ , R is $^ { \prime \prime } { + } 2 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { T } 2 = 2 7 . 9 5 - 2 7 . 4 - ( + 2 ) / 1 0 0 \mathsf { m m }$ $= 2 7 . 9 5 - 2 7 . 4 - 0 . 0 2 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 5 3 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(3) Select the reverse gear shim(s) (T2).

# BACKLASH(REGULAR ROTATION MODELS)

# NOTE:

• Do not install the water pump components when measuring the backlash.   
• Measure both the forward and reverse gear backlashes.   
• If both the forward and reverse gear backlashes are larger than specification, the pinion may be too high.   
• If both the forward and reverse gear backlashes are smaller than specification, the pinion may be too low.

![](images/97f2de534921ff09b66773f074450bacf711dce751955ac1a4d2a4cfb50e553c.jpg)

![](images/e263df5a82547308f96afba2563d847b7ce7aa8304946c37bc4760f5a047fa39.jpg)

# MEASURING THE FORWARD GEAR BACKLASH

1. Measure: • Forward gear backlash Out of specification Adjust.

![](images/1685809873bcd3ec827d1b95d9b933c20a46aa38e99aaa6a8ba7b6404be89eca.jpg)

Forward gear backlash 0.20 - 0.31 mm (0.008 - 0.012 in)

# Measuring steps

(1) Set the shift rod into the neutral position.

<table><tr><td>s</td><td>Shift rod wrench YB-06052 / 90890-06052</td></tr></table>

(2) Install the propeller shaft housing puller so it pushes against the propeller shaft.

![](images/4a43ff7b7f452f634866b5f4ffd18c37ff456e4f0fcad260cfc4fc30e6a58bcf.jpg)

<table><tr><td></td><td>Center bolt 10 Nm (1.0 m • kgf, 7.2 ft • Ib)</td></tr></table>

![](images/b679a1c9582c2f9fb23b8aac56001d8920b7dc3989b9f0f9e4bc06428611fde6.jpg)

(3) Install the backlash indicator onto the drive shaft (on the $2 2 . 4 ~ \mathsf { m m }$ (0.88 in) diameter portion of the drive shaft).

![](images/2494d4b8441a6041b0e861c042bbd13c51a6a9f83a8fb87dd2884f6943f4ef16.jpg)

(4) Install the dial gauge onto the lower unit and have the dial gauge plunger contact the mark on the backlash indicator.

![](images/18a7cfd856ee8a844ac4070b5e7e9e8328b7615787d9ef8e19b1219a0415ac58.jpg)

![](images/5504516c65fbcf68b030da41bafa647174e8e64210f0c9dec7ff9adb05f1e763.jpg)

(5) Set the lower unit upside down.

(6) Slowly turn the drive shaft clockwise and counterclockwise. When the drive shaft stops in each direction, measure the backlash.

2. Adjust:

• Forward gear shim Remove or add shim(s).

M: Measurement

![](images/84a9ab9b7fb63d8c4879719bae9ca1e489109d9cea901b16e36dc6e07b5e0fae.jpg)

(5) Set the lower unit upside down.   
(6) Slowly turn the drive shaft clockwise and counterclockwise. When the drive shaft stops in each direction, measure the backlash.

If the $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 0 0 + ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ = 1.00 + 0.05 mm = 1.05 mm   
If $" { \sf P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is $\mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 3 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { M } 0 \ = \ 1 . 0 0 + ( - 3 ) / 1 0 0 \ \mathsf { m m }$ $= 1 . 0 0 - 0 . 0 3 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 9 7 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

# NOTE:

$\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume an $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

Example:

# SHIMMING (COUNTER ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

![](images/d9f3618efd1b48f52f060e2bb4d116c9685f27628f7b04f647c4a5ee8251d721.jpg)

(5) Calculate the pinion shim thickness (T3).

Pinion shim thickness (T3) = 62.5 + P/100 – M3 – M4

# NOTE:

“P” is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $" \mathsf { P } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# Example:

If M3 is $^ { \prime \prime } 4 6 . 8 5 \mathrm { \ m m ^ { \prime \prime } }$ , M4 is $^ { \prime \prime } 1 5 . 1 2 \mathsf { m m } ^ { \prime \prime }$ and   
P is $\mathtt { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } - 5 \mathit { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
T3 = 62.5 + (–5)/100 – 46.85 – 15.12 mm $= 6 2 . 5 - 0 . 0 5 - 4 6 . 8 5 - 1 5 . 1 2 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 4 8 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(6) Select the pinion shim(s) (T3).

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Calculated numeralat 1/100th place</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>Roundednumeral</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>More than</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>or less</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.00</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.00</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.10</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=3>V Available shim thickness0.10, 0.12, 0.15, 0.18, 0.30, 0.40and 0.50 mm</td></tr></table>

# SHIMMING (COUNTER ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

![](images/d5518699b041339317dc28fabceeedc29ac911d39c125ff777c519c176d46fdf.jpg)

# SELECTING THE REVERSE GEAR SHIMS

# NOTE:

Select the shim thickness (T1) by using the specified measurement(s) and the calculation formula.

Select: • Shim thickness (T1)

Selecting steps (1) Measure (M1).

<table><tr><td></td><td>Digital caliper 90890-06704</td></tr></table>

![](images/c456e0158f3fe2443a9a568f1cbc78a0840110bc11319bdac6f9f4279df6e65b.jpg)

# NOTE:

• Measure the combined thickness of the roller bearing $\textcircled{1}$ and thrust bearing $\textcircled{2}$ . • Turn the roller bearing outer race two or three times so the rollers seat. Then, measure the height of the bearing, as shown. • Perform the same measurement at three points on the roller bearing outer race. • Find the average of the measurements (M1).

![](images/35cded3e456456c21951271b753fa4ea531f6f05773df393ffcb3b44c543f94d.jpg)

(2) Calculate the reverse gear shim thickness (T1).

![](images/5ae0bb73a6b9b41b194955f944f65d5ddd7702402b3cbce8c00843cf257127b6.jpg)

# Reverse gear shim thickness (T1) (T1) = 25.3 + F/100 – M1

# NOTE:

$" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - } \mathsf { m m }$ units. If the $" \digamma ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume an “F” value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# SHIMMING (COUNTER ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

Example:

If M1 is $^ { \prime \prime } 2 4 . 8 0 \ : \mathsf { m m } ^ { \prime \prime }$ and F is $\prime 5 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { T } 1 = 2 5 . 3 + ( + 5 ) / 1 0 0 - 2 4 . 8 0 \mathsf { m m }$ $= 2 5 . 3 + 0 . 0 5 - 2 4 . 8 0 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 5 5 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(3) Select the reverse gear shim(s).

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Calculated numeralat 1/100th place</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>Roundednumeral</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>More than</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>or less</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.00</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.00</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.02</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.05</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.10</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>0.08</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=3>V Available shim thickness0.10, 0.12, 0.15, 0.18, 0.30, 0.40and 0.50 mm</td></tr></table>

![](images/b001226b52cc840ef38e40649f32db67166ecca0411d9cd4bb0329fecaad2d9a.jpg)

# SELECTING THE FORWARD GEAR SHIMS

NOTE:

Select the shim thickness (T2) by using the specified measurement(s) and the calculation formula.

Select: • Shim thickness (T2)

Selecting steps (1) Measure (M2).

![](images/35cdcf48f7f2283770011b9e3f7792871287764cfb953172c775774214d216c8.jpg)

# NOTE:

• Measure the height of the gear as shown.   
• Perform the same measurement at three points on the gear.   
• Find the average of the measurements (M2).

# SHIMMING (COUNTER ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

![](images/d55d81e9d3b5c69af2ecebb66efcbaca8cf4b6547f60c2ae8e7e1cbfcb5f5a72.jpg)

(2) Calculate the forward gear shim thickness (T2).

Forward gear shim thickness (T2) = M2 – 28.1 – R/100

# NOTE:

$\mathbf { \chi } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { \cal { R } } ^ { \prime \prime }$ is the deviation of the lower case dimension from standard. It is stamped on the trim tab mounting surface of the lower case in $0 . 0 1 \mathrm { - m m }$ units. If the $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ mark is missing or unreadable, assume a $\mathbf { \Omega } ^ { \prime \prime } \mathbf { R } ^ { \prime \prime }$ value of $" 0 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , and check the backlash when the unit is assembled.

# Example:

If M2 is $^ { \prime \prime } 2 9 . 1 0 \mathrm { m m } ^ { \prime \prime }$ , R is $^ { \prime \prime } { + } 2 ^ { \prime \prime }$ , then   
$\mathsf { T } 2 = 2 9 . 1 0 - 2 8 . 1 - ( + 2 ) / 1 0 0 \mathsf { m m }$ $= 2 9 . 1 0 - 2 8 . 1 - 0 . 0 2 \ : \mathrm { m m }$ $= 0 . 9 8 ~ \mathrm { m m }$

(3) Select the forward gear shim(s) (T2).

# SHIMMING (COUNTER ROTATION MODELS) (FOR WORLDWIDE)

![](images/a734335dc575f95695b39c2f2582eb2a35da4527e2ed6e6365d105de66ecaf63.jpg)

![](images/da0719f4dd7c1a7ef7e285a645e3cf76e8e3b27241fa08c065c37983b4790521.jpg)

![](images/d067fff9d6fbe7f7b2e626543b0f0a816c67805647a9aea1d28cc10975fc6ac5.jpg)

# SELECTING THE PROPELLER SHAFT SHIMS

NOTE:

Find the shim thickness (T4) by selecting shims until the specified measurement is obtained with the special tool.

1. Install:

• Shim(s) 1 • Thrust bearing $\textcircled{2}$ • Propeller shaft $\textcircled{3}$ • Tapered roller bearing $\textcircled{4}$

2. Measure:

• Propeller shaft free play Out of specification Adjust.

![](images/5787e4d08c96abc987c41ed733dd9207cc571f277a7123704cdfd0821158491a.jpg)

3. Adjust:

• Propeller shaft free play Remove or add shim(s).

![](images/88bd24ae1e543c174dfac84a853cf78d6a1b5a5e110cac75bc38c5ab502ff5e5.jpg)

Available shim thickness 0.10, 0.12, 0.15, 0.18, 0.30, 0.40 and 0.50 mm

# BACKLASH(COUNTER ROTATION MODELS)

# NOTE:

• Do not install the water pump components when measuring the backlash.   
• Measure both the forward and reverse gear backlashes.   
• If both the forward and reverse gear backlashes are larger than specification, the pinion may be too high.   
• If both the forward and reverse gear backlashes are smaller than specification, the pinion may be too low.

![](images/6295ed78a35d16aa8d367b8e575f7a976417192cbb4b0b753beae0dd74eb20b8.jpg)

![](images/e19a04f2f644381371be1608361c193df69fc7c43a78b028ff55ba1a8981e1e4.jpg)

# MEASURING THE FORWARD GEAR BACKLASH

1. Measure: • Forward gear backlash Out of specification Adjust.

![](images/403737a386571187ad9c2382a4f03ed8b74fc8428c998988a1cc82910a77b4ec.jpg)

Forward gear backlash 0.15 - 0.30 mm (0.006 - 0.012 in)

# Measuring steps

(1) Set the shift rod into the neutral position.

<table><tr><td>s</td><td>Shift rod wrench YB-06052 / 90890-06052</td></tr></table>

(2) Install the propeller shaft housing puller so it pushes against the propeller shaft.

![](images/8c9fe1579903ce712c577fab542a78daa55cd844c9f7850073452bdb1998a130.jpg)

<table><tr><td></td><td>Center bolt 10 Nm (1.0 m • kgf, 7.2 ft • Ib)</td></tr></table>

![](images/2e7f569406a7ff33a16891d25899a20485ca58633d778b73864b2aa50d622c66.jpg)

(3) Install the backlash indicator onto the drive shaft (on the $2 2 . 4 ~ \mathsf { m m }$ (0.88 in) diameter portion of the drive shaft).

![](images/c9132f60d56ae4c1ac1e41baa98faa0cba9de485f312d1c8502c4bd442ce7caa.jpg)

(4) Install the dial gauge onto the lower unit and have the dial gauge plunger contact the mark on the backlash indicator.

![](images/f9ba242ac79bc0ba4f12a76ab7572113c5a86e0d8eb67cb877678dd64bdd1011.jpg)

![](images/040f7b7f55418f52e8507ecab39285955843a352389926114ebc84902c76e343.jpg)

(5) Set the lower unit upside down.

(6) Slowly turn the drive shaft clockwise and counterclockwise. When the drive shaft stops in each direction, measure the backlash.

2. Adjust:

• Forward gear shim Remove or add shim(s).

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>公</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Forward gearbacklash</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Shim thickness</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>Less than0.15 mm (0.006 in)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>To be increased by(0.23 – M) × 0.58</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2>More than0.30 mm (0.012 in)</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>To be decreased by(M – 0.23) × 0.58</td></tr></table>

M: Measurement

# MEASURING THE REVERSE GEAR BACKLASH

1. Measure: • Reverse gear backlash Out of specification Adjust.

<table><tr><td></td><td>Reverse gear backlash 0.5 - 0.7 mm (0.020 - 0.028 in)</td></tr></table>

![](images/a404d8215097aa6cba12559a166ed4b74048960734b7994d322160dc6ce68ba5.jpg)

![](images/96f0c752e3c4d60c7e94fc9c73da84a43b00a27382d1a6cc34ba43a951403030.jpg)

# Measuring steps

(1) Set the shift rod into the neutral position.

# Shift rod wrench YB-06052 / 90890-06052

(2) Load the reverse gear by installing the propeller without the spacer and then tighten the propeller nut.

# Propeller nut 5 Nm (0.5 m • kgf, 3.6 ft • lb)

(3) Install the backlash indicator onto the drive shaft (on the $2 2 . 4 ~ \mathsf { m m }$ (0.88 in) diameter portion of the drive shaft).

# Backlash indicator . YB-06265 / 90890-06706

(4) Install the dial gauge onto the lower unit and have the dial gauge plunger contact the mark on the backlash indicator.

![](images/75b53863f4b2d44cdb9a970327b3a918f7fe035ccaef515719b0b01e986af60b.jpg)

![](images/0c427175f1a8ae61d974eee38c1795a4fec2da71ae8b16d8f1727bf14d4efe07.jpg)

![](images/0fc94275a274463038cdb0bf7ea26cac1d66bf0d8c909b7439e0ec2cca02cc7f.jpg)

![](images/6b61c3eca03d39fe66f6792ef5af8b669a634a2f16e3691958f70eb3e064a2ce.jpg)

(5) Set the lower unit upside down.   
(6) Turn the shift rod into the reverse position with the shift rod wrench.   
(7) Turn the drive shaft clockwise until the clutch dog is fully engaged.   
(8) Turn the shift rod into the neutral position with the shift rod wrench.   
(9) Turn the drive shaft counterclockwise approximately $30 ^ { \circ }$ more.

![](images/b8569ac6a5e2bdc9f7e68a317cbf4c493aac5e1cfe2307fd8355f6385d82d459.jpg)

(10) Turn the shift rod into the reverse position with the shift rod wrench.

(11) Slowly turn the drive shaft clockwise and counterclockwise. When the drive shaft stops in each direction, measure the backlash.

# NOTE:

When measuring the reverse gear backlash, turn the shift rod wrench towards the reverse position with force.

# 2. Adjust:

• Reverse gear shim Remove or add shim(s).

<table><tr><td></td><td>Reverse gear backlash</td><td>Shim thickness</td></tr><tr><td>Less than 0.5 mm (0.020 in)</td><td></td><td>To be decreased by (0.6 − M) × 0.58</td></tr><tr><td>More than 0.7 mm (0.028 in)</td><td></td><td>To be increased by (M – 0.6) × 0.58</td></tr></table>

M: Measurement
