# POWER TRIM AND TILT UNITREMOVING/INSTALLING THE POWER TRIM AND TILT UNIT

![](images/ba8fe33fb1ef5fb1607f185a5f0b9a3a5491b06a4afd3d86752f0a315129b116.jpg)

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Order</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Job/Part</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Q&#x27;ty</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Remarks</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>123456</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>Tilt up the outboardPower trim and tilt leadPlastic locking tieBoltGround leadCirclipUpper mounting pin</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>2311</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>Not reusableContinued on next page.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>11</td></tr></table>

![](images/0401c9ec4035decd34f9a7933fdf9904829e7357367a6d57ec4b7130d4550346.jpg)

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Order</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Job/Part</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Q&#x27;ty</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Remarks</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>7891011</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>BoltWasherLower mounting pinPower trim and tilt unitCollar</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>2</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>For installation, reverse the removalprocedure.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>2116</td></tr></table>

![](images/2108eebbe779e65883504404843c2afa50f4965e30128a116e49adf505bb651b.jpg)

![](images/7e96cd6c6a069f79aa933c775aa72abe770d5be8b3ba5fa36d3040db22f60a82.jpg)

# WARNING

# REMOVING THE POWER TRIM AND TILT UNIT

After tilting up the outboard, be sure to support it with the tilt stop levers. Otherwise, the outboard could suddenly lower if the power trim and tilt unit should lose fluid pressure.

# NOTE:

Tilt up the outboard and then turn the tilt stop levers $\textcircled{1}$ to support it.

Remove: • Power trim and tilt unit

# NOTE:

Slightly lower the tilt ram assembly and then remove the power trim and tilt unit.

# BLEEDING THE POWER TRIM AND TILT UNIT

NOTE:   
Install the power trim and tilt unit onto the outboard before bleeding.

# Bleed:

• Air bubbles (from the power trim and tilt unit)

# Bleeding steps

(1) Connect the battery leads to the battery.

(2) Loosen the manual valve $\textcircled{1}$ by turning it counterclockwise until it stops.

![](images/215b8340a31077a893897f6224ce3b245b5a81f89daf3e6b9b8eac13685be7ba.jpg)

![](images/050ca9355b149c98833ee288a85a41ddb27229c406fde0348962ddcea0afa6d4.jpg)

(3) Tilt up the outboard fully, then release it, and let it lower by its own weight.   
(4) Tighten the manual valve by turning it clockwise.   
(5) Let the power trim and tilt fluid settle for about 5 minutes.   
(6) Push and hold the power trim and tilt switch in the up position until the outboard is fully tilted up.   
(7) Turn the tilt stop levers to support the outboard. Then, let the power trim and tilt fluid settle for about 5 minutes.   
(8) Remove the reservoir cap $\textcircled{2}$ and check that fluid is up to the brim as shown. Add fluid if the level is below the brim.   
(9) Install the power trim and tilt reservoir cap.   
(10) Repeat the above steps two or three times until the power trim and tilt fluid is at the correct level.

# RESERVOIR AND POWER TRIM AND TILT MOTOR REMOVING/INSTALLING THE RESERVOIR AND POWER TRIM AND TILT MOTOR

![](images/3432b7ffa76cd9b8dc292c781c02eebd729fde8c5c2044aca5b81192bf796212.jpg)

<table><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Order</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=4>Job/Part</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Q&#x27;ty</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>Remarks</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=4 colspan=1>12</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=4>Power trim and tilt unitReservoir cap</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td><td rowspan=11 colspan=1>Refer to &quot;POWER TRIM AND TILT UNIT&quot;on page 7-29.For installation, reverse the removalprocedure.</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=3 colspan=2>Bolt</td><td></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=2></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=2></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>3</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>3</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=3>Reservoir</td><td rowspan=4 colspan=2>ReservoirBoltPower trim and tilt motorO-ring</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=3 colspan=1>456</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>4</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td></tr><tr><td></td><td></td><td></td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>7</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=4>Drive pin</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=2 colspan=1>8</td><td rowspan=2 colspan=4>Gear pump housing filter</td><td rowspan=1 colspan=1>1</td></tr><tr><td rowspan=1 colspan=1></td></tr></table>

# WARNING

• To prevent the hydraulic fluid from spurting out due to internal pressure, the outboard should be kept fully tilted up (the tilt rod at full length). • After removing the power trim and tilt motor or reservoir, do not push the tilt ram down. This may cause hydraulic fluid to spurt out from the port.

# CAUTION:

Do not wipe hydraulic system components with rags, paper, tissues, or the like, as fibers from such material will cause malfunctions if they enter the system.

# CHECKING THE RESERVOIR

1. Drain: • Power trim and tilt fluid   
2. Check: • Reservoir Cracks/damage/leaks Replace.

# CHECKING THE GEAR PUMP HOUSING FILTER

Check:

• Gear pump housing filter Damage/tears Replace. Foreign matter Clean.

![](images/9b6c7463168294a5dcd0a3b45508701a57c6cdb76559a20b4ee0740d80e04b40.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE POWER TRIM ANDTILT MOTOR

1. Install: • Gear pump housing filter $\textcircled{1}$ • Drive pin $\textcircled{2}$

2. Fill: • Gear pump housing

![](images/c2eedf92d02f8db0a2d10c43f7d23135dfd138dd0e436497bfda58bf73c00c21.jpg)

Recommended power trim and   
tilt fluid ATF Dexron II

# NOTE:

Add power trim and tilt fluid until it reaches the top of the gear pump housing.

![](images/7c7b62287ce2da5e6f328021c2ff73c682a16a7db868088a6db49f8dea3d369f.jpg)

3. Bleed: • Air bubbles

# NOTE:

![](images/f2e67f8531b0a743ab6f2d51155a396ed1b333476800fc1c6a9dff0a2b346527.jpg)

• Remove all of the air bubbles with a syringe or suitable tool as shown. • Turn the gear pump gears with a screwdriver and then remove any air between the gear teeth.

# 4. Install:

• O-ring 1   
• Power trim and tilt motor $\textcircled{2}$   
• Bolt $\textcircled{3}$

# NOTE:

Align the armature shaft with the recess in the drive pin.

# FILLING THE RESERVOIR

# WARNING

To prevent the hydraulic fluid from spurting out due to internal pressure, the tilt ram should be kept at full length.

1. Fill: • Reservoir

![](images/8cf01ebf96cbb95d0739bee1031ce5d899c42214f6023513c5811d8a61cdc898.jpg)

![](images/a34b615d085792ee50ca144cc587b8d45bc5830b9255f69d5e70619dcdd33ce9.jpg)

Recommended power trim and   
tilt fluid ATF Dexron II

2. Check:

• Power trim and tilt fluid level Level is $\mathsf { l o w } \to \mathsf { A d d }$ power trim and tilt fluid to the proper level.

# BLEEDING THE POWER TRIM AND TILT UNIT

# NOTE:

This bleeding must be done before installing the power trim and tilt unit onto the outboard.

1. Bleed:

![](images/8b8f0e6795b10c2fac2a01b1f4ef1b440f32acfe69ebe2e070c1645963df454c.jpg)

• Air bubbles (from the power trim and tilt unit)

![](images/d413eb2eb1289e4fcfe20dfda3664270244505668d6fe712434ff3f6fa2c3e0c.jpg)

# Bleeding steps

(1) Set the power trim and tilt unit upright.   
(2) Connect the leads of the power trim and tilt on the battery terminals until the trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully compressed.

# NOTE:

If the rams will not go down, refer to the following.

A. Connect the leads of the power trim and tilt on the battery terminals until the trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully extended. Then, reverse the leads on the battery terminals until the trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully compressed.

B. If step A was unsuccessful, connect the leads on the battery terminals and fully compress the tilt ram assembly by hand.   
C. If step B was unsuccessful, loosen the manual valve, compress the trim and tilt ram assemblies fully by hand, and then tighten the manual valve. Then, compress and extend the trim and tilt ram assemblies by connecting the leads on the battery terminals in the up and down positions.   
D. If step C was unsuccessful, disassemble, check, and correct any problems with the power trim and tilt unit.

![](images/bcd35192c720bc7aa18977378547304a893d506141b772c69c252cc75525907e.jpg)

(3) Connect the leads on the battery terminals in the up position until the trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully extended.

![](images/13cbd851e07a6e08189fe6cbe790aca7ae72db9c2d801dc090ecf8dbefe0393f.jpg)

(4) Remove the power trim and tilt reservoir cap and check that fluid is up to the brim as shown. Add power trim and tilt fluid if the level is below the brim.

(5) Repeat the above steps two or three times until the fluid is at the correct level.

2. Check:

• Power trim and tilt unit operation Unsmooth operation Bleed the power trim and tilt unit again.

# MEASURING THE HYDRAULIC PRESSURE

Check:

• Hydraulic pressure Out of specification Repair.

Hydraulic pressure   
(with the power trim and tilt ram   
assemblies fully extended) 9.8 - 11.8 MPa (100 - 120 kg/cm2)   
(with the power trim and tilt ram   
assemblies fully compressed) 5.9 - 8.8 MPa $( 6 0 - 9 0 \mathrm { k g } / \mathrm { c m } ^ { 2 } )$

![](images/3290f0104468422bba8a36ca91337bf2760bdd009e636bfca3a9b80bd89b22df.jpg)

![](images/cf8381d282e2fda8829b5d4be873d4d1a7617f7a793106b9168ff719e37b0fff.jpg)

# NOTE:

Before measuring the hydraulic pressure, bleed the power trim and tilt unit.

# Measuring steps

(1) Fully tilt up the power trim and tilt ram assemblies.   
(2) Remove the circlip $\textcircled{1}$ .   
(3) Remove the manual valve $\textcircled{2}$ and install the up-relief valve attachment and hydraulic pressure gauge and tighten them to the specified torque.

![](images/0ba84e53c7e345dfc3626161b1f6975b2ca60dbb4c81441ce52fd212f67dee96.jpg)

# NOTE:

Remove the manual valve and then quickly attach the special tools before any fluid comes out.

![](images/3fe56d93f7e7c720d462ba3dc487ebb530778c0e601c5f5937258cdb2acf5551.jpg)

![](images/e27101f7eb578d81c49b26f2610238ced5d0d856ef93d15e897babeabb5d3de3.jpg)

![](images/ec993a2acfcd4ad434109a97452b7d93e4d5dc27bb70890971a67124a5449200.jpg)

![](images/b2ccf574ecb4657cd2bef04f3ad1cfe6461fae5942758690042b30db3e852829.jpg)

(4) Connect the leads on the battery terminals in the down position until the power trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully compressed.

(5) Connect the leads on the battery terminals in the up position until the power trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully extended. Then, measure the hydraulic pressure.

![](images/e088e85bab6129d85939be27a691a31efadec01c58ef5592ca19a01ecfd811c4.jpg)

Hydraulic pressure   
(with the power trim and tilt ram   
assemblies fully extended) 9.8 - 11.8 MPa (100 - 120 kg/cm2)

(6) After measuring the hydraulic pressure, remove the special tools and quickly attach the down-relief valve attachment.

Hydraulic pressure gauge ........ 4 90890-06776   
Down-relief valve attachment. $\textcircled{5}$ 90890-06774

Hydraulic pressure gauge 9 Nm (0.9 m • kgf, 6.5 ft • lb) Down-relief valve attachment 4 Nm (0.4 m • kgf, 2.9 ft • lb)

(7) Remove the reservoir cap and check that fluid is up to the brim as shown. Add fluid if the level is below the brim.

(8) Install the reservoir cap.

(9) Connect the leads on the battery terminals in the down position until the power trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully compressed. Then, measure the hydraulic pressure.

![](images/5678ef3e921cc04e3a9ce7a27f29470be27ad3084f9548de8d4ff6c90715cd11.jpg)

Hydraulic pressure (with the power trim and tilt ram assemblies fully compressed) 5.9 - 8.8 MPa $( 6 0 - 9 0 \mathrm { k g } / \mathrm { c m } ^ { 2 } )$

![](images/dcfca348814aac257c1f60d6cfa9152921737c2aed7ad3349d51902788abbe69.jpg)

(10) After measuring the hydraulic pressure, connect the leads on the battery terminals in the up position until the power trim and tilt ram assemblies are fully extended.

(11) Remove the special tools.

(12) Install the manual valve and circlip.

# NOTE:

After measuring the hydraulic pressure, bleed the power trim and tilt unit.

# TILT RAM ASSEMBLY AND GEAR PUMP UNIT REMOVING/INSTALLING THE TILT RAM ASSEMBLY AND GEAR PUMP UNIT

![](images/a766f3bbfcaf9a04c34189854a353a0e1b4ccc0b6a54dcd8e3190c4ecb057cf7.jpg)

# REMOVING THE TILT RAM END SCREW

oosen: • Tilt ram end screw

NOTE:

Hold the power trim and tilt unit in a vise using aluminum plates on both sides.

# REMOVING THE GEAR PUMP UNIT

Remove:

• Bolt 1   
• Gear pump unit $\textcircled{2}$ • O-ring $\textcircled{3}$   
• Check valve 4

NOTE:

Place a container under the power trim and tilt unit.

![](images/7d098b7058dfe22446202869a19f0f61aa4cf945df34d822e59904bdec361d14.jpg)

# DISASSEMBLING THE GEAR PUMP UNIT

1. Remove: • Bolt $\textcircled{1}$ • Pump gear $\textcircled{2}$ • Up-relief valve assembly $\textcircled{3}$ • Ball $( 4 . 7 6 \ : \mathrm { m m } / 0 . 1 8 7$ in) $\textcircled{4}$ • Shuttle valve $\textcircled{5}$ • Ball $( 3 . 1 8 \ : \mathrm { m m } / 0 . 1 2 5 \ : \mathrm { i n } ) \textcircled { \div }$

NOTE:

When removing the pump gears, note their original direction and position for proper assembly.

![](images/6b404dd24eb31d21852d57da842668579492c5a4616b65a00a4c3dae489ff7ee.jpg)

2. Remove: • Check valves $\textcircled{1}$ and $\textcircled{2}$

# NOTE:

To remove the check valves, cover the gear pump housing with a clean cloth and then blow compressed air through holes $\textcircled{2}$ and $\textcircled{6}$ .

# CHECKING THE TILT RAM

Check:

• Tilt ram Excessive scratches Replace. Bends/excessive corrosion Replace. Rust Polish. (with $4 0 0 - 6 0 0$ grit sandpaper)

![](images/1734a7d895d184f0ceeb414331cb07fa2cde967a366208d983c60c1fd8a024da.jpg)

# CHECKING THE GEAR PUMP UNIT

Check:

• Shuttle valves $\textcircled{1}$   
• Check valve assemblies $\textcircled{2}$ Clogs/damage/wear Replace.   
• Pump gears $\textcircled{3}$ Damage/wear Replace the gear pump unit.   
• Up-relief valve assembly $\textcircled{4}$   
• Down-relief valve assembly $\textcircled{5}$ Damage/wear Replace the gear pump unit.   
• Balls $\textcircled{6}$ Damage/wear Replace.

# ASSEMBLING THE GEAR PUMP UNIT

# CAUTION:

Install all components in their original direction and position for proper assembly and operation.

![](images/e113b58cc02061a2b5ca724f85b3444b5da41582b7f89d4ae8fa596796a35e29.jpg)

# NOTE:

Apply grease to the balls to prevent them from falling out of the gear pump.

1. Install: • Balls $( 3 . 1 8 \ : \mathrm { m m } / 0 . 1 2 5 \ : \mathrm { i n } ) \textcircled { 1 }$ • Shuttle valves $\textcircled{2}$

![](images/1185a480acc134c3ccbcbf5adcac14bc3c178dcb80b8aad1270cbd9c0229889a.jpg)

2. Install:

• O-ring $\textcircled{1}$   
• Ball (3.18 mm/0.125 in) $\textcircled{2}$   
• Up-relief valve pin $\textcircled{3}$   
• Spring $\textcircled{4}$   
• Up-relief valve $\textcircled{5}$   
• Up-relief valve assembly $\textcircled{6}$

![](images/b93724275907d886533297cf374171d157095d842f5ec619ce5ce612e460d10a.jpg)

3. Install:

• O-rings $\textcircled{1}$   
• Check valves $\textcircled{2}$   
• Balls $( 4 . 7 6 \ : \mathrm { m m } / 0 . 1 8 7 \ : \mathrm { i n } ) \textcircled { 3 }$   
• Pump gears $\textcircled{4}$

![](images/49484a9e907fb0b89431c0d50695e4c2cd1e0c13c2ed0f6826a4e6effa13392c.jpg)

4. Install:

• Gear pump $\textcircled{1}$   
• Bolt $\textcircled{2}$   
• Filter $\textcircled{3}$   
• O-ring $\textcircled{4}$   
• Down-relief valve $\textcircled{5}$   
• Filter $\textcircled{6}$

NOTE:

Tighten the bolts evenly and make sure the pump gears turn smoothly.

![](images/1988faebe4afb064b5aaa5643d9367b3e9453aeb29b259e497a0d61faf6d3bc1.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE GEAR PUMP UNIT

![](images/f7a34a19a59a45ba6f65395f44affe1741d7d6e8ad22da648894969dc79f2643.jpg)

Install:   
• O-rings 1   
• Ball $\textcircled{2}$   
• Pin 3   
• Check valve $\textcircled{4}$   
• Check valve assembly $\textcircled{5}$

# NOTE:

When installing the check valve assembly, make sure the pin is on the tilt ram cylinder side as shown.

2. Install:

• Gear pump unit $\textcircled{1}$ • Bolt $\textcircled{2}$

# INSTALLING THE TILT RAMASSEMBLY

# WARNING

To prevent the hydraulic fluid from spurting out due to internal pressure, the tilt ram should be kept at full length.

tilt fluid ATF Dexron II

![](images/2c4ac9820d30d693401b03c73332ec90e84dceed7e06efcdbe0f8dc4a5253634.jpg)

tilt fluid ATF Dexron II

# REMOVING THE FREE PISTON

1. Drain: • Power trim and tilt fluid

NOTE:

After removing the trim ram assemblies, drain the fluid from the power trim and tilt unit.

2. Install: • Trim ram assemblies 1

NOTE:   
Finger-tighten the trim ram assemblies and then cover the tilt cylinder openings with a clean cloth.

3. Remove: • Free piston 2

# WARNING

Never look into the tilt cylinder opening because the free piston and hydraulic fluid may be expelled out forcefully.

NOTE:

Remove the free piston by blowing compressed air through the hole $\textcircled{2}$ .

![](images/fc3e9fe515c65b053cec4d0adec1132d917be2f909696f0ec3f638c4bcc9ff4c.jpg)

# ELECTRICAL COMPONENTS ANALYSIS DIGITAL CIRCUIT TESTER

<table><tr><td>008</td><td>Digital tester J-39299 / 90890-06752</td></tr></table>

NOTE:   
“ ” indicates a continuity of electricity which means a closed circuit at the respective switch position.

# MEASURING THE PEAK VOLTAGE

# NOTE:

• When checking the condition of the ignition system it is useful to know the peak   
voltage.   
• Cranking speed is dependant on many factors (e.g., fouled or weak spark plugs, a weak battery). If one of these is defective, the peak voltage will be lower than specification.   
• If the peak voltage measurement is not within specification the engine will not operate properly.

![](images/529c0badcec1c81469586594f0a6cf72bf660df9ff482628d411cd9d867a9512.jpg)

# PEAK VOLTAGE ADAPTOR

NOTE: The peak voltage adaptor should be used with the digital circuit tester.

<table><tr><td>8</td><td>Peak voltage adaptor YU-39991/ 90890-03169</td></tr></table>

![](images/e349fc31ef3a72f5285d8d3b4d190e399eb63bb2076b0b01741ad7f6a858c3ab.jpg)

# NOTE:

• When measuring the peak voltage, set the selector to the DC voltage mode.   
• Make sure the peak voltage adaptor leads are properly installed in the digital tester.   
• Make sure the positive pin (the $" + "$ mark facing up as shown) on the peak voltage adaptor is installed into the positive terminal of the digital tester.   
• The test harness is needed for the following tests.

![](images/93a89b4a19ba1b6bb6e2c86aa4d19e7f16f15ef342329d6ac74fc3150917d7e4.jpg)

# Measuring steps

(1) Disconnect the coupler connections.   
(2) Connect the test harness between the couplers.   
(3) Connect the peak voltage adaptor probes to the connectors which are being checked.   
(4) Start or crank the engine and observe the measurement.

# MEASURING A LOW RESISTANCE

When measuring a resistance of $\boldsymbol { 1 0 } \ \Omega$ or less with the digital tester, the correct measurement cannot be obtained because of the tester’s internal resistance. To obtain the correct value, subtract the internal resistance from the displayed measurement.

![](images/0533329fc11e371afe1de3106dcea5c18f4206e120c4837022c96f82a22e2dd9.jpg)

# NOTE:

The internal resistance of the digital tester can be obtained by connecting both of its probes.

![](images/12c6c214b6f9ceab9801a9014d07a65417aad7c285c57e9365791e9c638b109e.jpg)

# CHECKING THE IGNITION SPARK GAP8

• Do not touch any of the connections of the spark gap tester lead wires. • Do not let sparks leak out of the removed spark plug cap. • Keep flammable gas or liquids away, since this test can produce sparks.

Check:

• Ignition spark gap   
Above specification Replace the spark plug.   
Below specification Check the ECM output.

![](images/e64c76d26a124c80f4461c698f8cee914d9335f011ec151cf4e2d8a24f48b986.jpg)

# Ignition spark gap 1.0 - 1.1 mm (0.039 - 0.043 in)

Å For USA and Canada ı For worldwide

![](images/f8284ea8f740e7c4a9f316f3c77effb3589de906c0dbf759246658a9e3c95e9e.jpg)

![](images/ef29cbe87bfbddf5572153414c7b42b7b7a28c4e2420586abdf9b56aea15d44c.jpg)

# Checking steps

(1) Remove the spark plugs from the engine.   
(2) Connect a spark plug cap to the spark gap tester.   
(3) Set the spark gap length on the adjusting knob.

# Spark gap tester YM-34487 / 90890-06754

(4) Crank the engine and observe the spark through the discharge window of the spark gap tester.

# MEASURING THE IGNITION SYSTEM PEAK VOLTAGE

# WARNING

When checking the peak voltage do not touch any of the connections of the digital tester lead wires.

# NOTE:

• If there is no spark or the spark is weak, continue with the ignition system test. • If a good spark is obtained, the problem is not with the ignition system, but possibly with the spark plug(s) or another component.

![](images/9dc6be8c5a694749ab7bbbd7a8daf9d761bdaba7f1774859265db25da9c6eec3.jpg)

1. Measure:

# NOTE:

• The peak voltage adaptor should be used with the digital circuit tester. • When measuring the peak voltage, set the selector to the DC voltage mode.

# MEASURING THE ENGINE COOLING WATER TEMPERATURE SENSOR RESISTANCE

Measure:

• Engine cooling water temperature sensor resistance Out of specification Replace.

Engine cooling water   
temperature sensor resistance Black/yellow (B/Y) – Black (B) 5 ˚C (41 ˚F): 4.62 kΩ 20 ˚C (68 ˚F): 2.44 kΩ 100 ˚C (212 ˚F): 0.19 kΩ

# Measuring steps

(1) Place the engine cooling water temperature sensor in a container filled with water.

(2) Place a thermometer in the water.

(3) Slowly heat the water.

(4) Measure the resistance when the specified temperature is reached.

![](images/8df27633d276c70978e9f428edd20eccab688482d6f7ebf2d4036da27c4ff325.jpg)

# CHECKING THE OIL PRESSURE SWITCH CONTINUITY

Measure: • Oil pressure switch continuity Out of specification Replace.

![](images/d2c1ba36c84f0dfcc7e03b4a5afa395def51ae757ad02db068c945c1caa43733.jpg)

Oil pressure switch continuity   
pressure 150 kPa ( $1 . 5 \mathrm { k g } / \mathrm { c m } ^ { 2 }$ , 21.33 psi) and below

![](images/d11b46fadb6af51fa1aafb1f896c9c5b144dd64fe54e24061d185f6b104071c2.jpg)

# MEASURING THE THROTTLE POSITION SENSOR

# NOTE:

When measuring the output voltage, set the selector to the DC voltage mode.

# Measure:

• Throttle position sensor output voltage Out of specification Adjust the throttle position sensor. Refer to “ADJUSTING THE THROTTLE POSITION SENSOR” on page 3-7.

![](images/00bac5fb399694a8761edd7babf5c8da2c111c1785e68a2db349977d733bac8a.jpg)

# Measuring steps

(1) Connect the test harness (3-pin) as shown.

# Test harness (3-pin) 90890-06793

(2) Connect the battery leads to a 12-V battery.   
(3) Turn the engine switch to the on position.   
(4) Measure the throttle position sensor output voltage.   
(5) Start the engine and measure the output voltage again.

# NOTE:

Make sure the throttle position sensor output voltage is within specification when the throttle is fully closed and fully opened.

# CHECKING THE FUEL INJECTORS

1. Check:

• Fuel injector operating sound No sound (no fuel is being sprayed) Check the high-pressure fuel pump.

# Checking steps

(1) Start the engine.   
(2) Fully close the throttle valves.   
(3) Attach the screwdriver $\textcircled{1}$ onto the fuel injector body and check if all of the fuel injectors have a solenoid valve operating sound.

2. Check:

• High-pressure fuel pump operating   
sound   
Correct Replace the fuel injector (no sound).   
No sound Check the main relay.

![](images/83e8daf28ebe4325250dcf03a3ae843e853d1e4603c83ec7c370e0d9e8e92796.jpg)

# NOTE:

• The high-pressure fuel pump should sound when the engine start switch is turned on.   
• Disconnect the Brown (Br) starter relay lead $\textcircled{1}$ to prevent the engine from starting.

![](images/f1f3f25c45257dac7c4d729971b9f7849fd21e28dafb14f34b0ef0c694d877e5.jpg)

3. Check:

• Main relay continuity Out of specification Replace the main relay.

# CHECKING THE MAGNETIC SWITCH RELAY

Check:

• Magnetic switch relay continuity Out of specification Replace.

# Checking steps

(1) Remove the terminal $\textcircled{1}$ from the magnetic switch relay.

# NOTE:

Remove the terminal to prevent the pinion gear from turning.

(2) Connect the tester leads between the magnetic switch relay terminals as shown.   
(3) Connect the Brown/white $( \mathsf { B r } / \mathsf { W } )$ lead to the positive battery terminal.   
(4) Connect the starter motor body to the negative battery terminal.

# CAUTION:

Do not connect the battery for more than one second. Otherwise, the magnetic switch relay may be damaged.

(5) Check that there is continuity between the magnetic switch relay terminals. (6) Check that there is no continuity after the Br/W lead is removed.

# NOTE:

The starter motor pinion should be pushed out while the magnetic switch is on.

(7) Install the terminal to the magnetic switch relay.

![](images/12b3c7817da7d929dcfa2e0e0d33aeeaf4ac9f1f631e590cb45dc81be77ac03f.jpg)

$\textcircled{1}$ Stator coil $\textcircled{2}$ Rectifier/regulator $\textcircled{3}$ Fuse (30A) $\textcircled{4}$ Battery

# REMOVING THE STATOR

Remove: • Stator 1

# CAUTION:

• Keep the power trim and tilt motor leads inside the stator.   
• Do not allow grease or oil to contact the commutator.

# NOTE:

• Remove the lead holder $\textcircled{2}$ and rubber spacer $\textcircled{3}$ from the stator and slide them towards the leads. • Hold the end of the armature shaft with a clean cloth and pull off the stator.

![](images/b276b72ca3b40e50416f47c08383cf70a7e507f3e517848e67f5fa7c3ca0a84a.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE BRUSH

Install:

• Brushes $\textcircled{1}$   
• Brush holders $\textcircled{2}$   
• Power trim and tilt motor leads $\textcircled{3}$   
• Screw $\textcircled{4}$

# CAUTION:

Do not touch the bimetal; touching it may affect the operation of the breaker.

![](images/38b8bbe593cd9c36315376a61319d9f33dc1b2935140aaae225ade8e92be3f10.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE ARMATURE

nstall: • Armature 1

# NOTE:

Push the brushes into the holder and then install the armature.

![](images/979334f5437109e5a9f0773831349b269def25a0b7a2c2cf556a9bcec026c619.jpg)

# INSTALLING THE STATOR

nstall: • Stator 1

# NOTE:

Place a clean cloth over the end of the armature shaft and carefully push the armature into the stator with a pair of pliers as shown.

# CHAPTER 9

# TROUBLE ANALYSIS

TROUBLE ANALYSIS. . 9-1   
TROUBLE ANALYSIS CHART . 9-1   
SELF-DIAGNOSIS.. .. 9-5   
DIAGNOSIS CODE INDICATION. . 9-5   
DIAGNOSIS THE ELECTRONIC CONTROL SYSTEM . 9-5

TROUBLE SHOOTING FOR ELECTRIC FUEL INJECTION... .. 9-7

# TROUBLE ANALYSIS

# NOTE:

The following items should be checked before the “TROUBLE ANALYSIS CHART” is consulted.

1. The battery is charged and its specified gravity is within specification.

2. There are no incorrect wiring connections.

3. Wiring connections are properly secured and are not rusty.

4. The lanyard is installed onto the engine stop switch.

5. The shift position is in neutral.

6. Fuel is reaching the vapor separator.

7. The rigging and engine setting are correct.

8. The engine is free from any “Hull problem”.

# SELF-DIAGNOSIS DIAGNOSIS CODE INDICATION

1. Normal condition (no defective part or irregular processing is found) Single flash is given every 4.95 seconds. $\textcircled{2}$ : Light on, 0.33 second $\textcircled{6}$ : Light off, 4.95 seconds

2. Trouble code indication Example: The illustration indicates code number 23.

$\textcircled{2}$ : Light on, 0.33 second $\textcircled{6}$ : Light off, 0.33 second $\circledcirc$ : Light off, 1.65 seconds $\textcircled{8}$ : Light off, 4.95 seconds

# DIAGNOSIS THE ELECTRONIC CONTROL SYSTEM

1. Install: • Diagnostic indicator

![](images/6749edcf13ab872df8a0b8684567902eae0ab4223b2b4126f0021ba6c434c096.jpg)

NOTE:

When performing this diagnosis, all of the electrical wires must be properly connected.

2. Check:

• Diagnosis code Code 1 is indicated Normal. Code 13 - 29 indicated Check the applicable parts. Code 33 - 44 indicated Replace the CDI unit.
